<Author>robandlil
<Content>Westin is great for Starpoints Just got back from Easter week at the Westin Rio Mar. We booked the hotel on points thru Starwood which was great. I used Trip Advisor hints extensively, so I wanted to report back on how it went.We rented a car from Avis at the airport for about $200 for the week which gave us flexiblitiy and savings. This was cheaper then using hotel transport which is $75 pp/each way. When we got to the hotel we used the open air staff parking across from the basement self park of the hotel. Again this saved us $10 a night for self park or $20 a night for valet park. When we arrived at the hotel at 2:30 our room was not ready, as we knew to expect from previous postings, so we had bathing suits and flip flops available, changed in the bathroom and hit the beach. By 4:00 we really wanted to check in, so got back on line. (this hotel does not have a starwood express line as it should) We were told our room still wasn't ready. When I pointed out that check in was supposed to be at 3, I was told that they have a window from 3 to 5. As I found this unacceptable, I announced that we would now wait at the lobby bar with complimentary drinks from them and that when the room was ready they could call us at the bar. The clerk said just one moment - went into the office for a minute- and came out announcing that our room was now ready. We asked for and received an upper floor with ocean view. The room was a little shabby, with cracked floor tiles and chipped tub, not as modern as the Westin in Cancun. But it was scrupulously clean and perfectly acceptable. Especially as it was free. The safe was still locked from previous guests, the refrigerator I had requested was not there, and the room key did not work. I stopped a passing security man, who apparently made a call for us and all was fixed within a half hour.We had stopped at Rodriquez' market on the corner of 3 as you turn to go on the road for the Westin as recommended on this site. This worked out well. We stocked up on soda, juice, chips, cookies and milk. This rounded out the hotel meals and meals out.In the room is a snack/drink frdge that is locked. We never unlocked it as I had read that the prices were ridiculous. There are 2 kinds of water in the room, large bottles with a private label from a local spring water company. These are free and I asked the maid to leave us extra each day which she did. I stored these in the fridge, and brought them down to the beach along with my insulated mug full of ice. This This worked out well. The bar refilled my mug with ice whenever I asked. Tere are also small bottles of water labelled Westin in the room. These are $3 each which you are not told. Most people were walking around with the Westin water - I think they wrongly thought that was the free one. There was a coffee maker with supplies (free) in the room as well as bathrobes.The hotel was full, and preferred seating at the pool and beach was hard to come by. There are two pools. Only the quiet pool has chairs with cushions. This was my biggest complaint. It is hard to sit all day on fake plastic wicker beach chairs. So by about 9:00 the best chairs at the pools (under umbrellas) and at the beach in the shade were already reserved. My husband went down at 7 each morning to put towels and magazines on the chairs in the shade that we wanted. At 8 you can wait on line for a worker to set up an umbrella on the beach for you. People who came down at 11 were out of luck for chairs or umbrella's. We saw a lot of angry people. However, I will remind you that this was Easter week and probably if you go at any other week it wouldn't be so cutthroat.

<Author>jlb3
<Content>Typical beach resort My fiance and I read the other reviews on TripAdvisor prior to booking our trip over Easter weekend to this venue. I would say that most of the other reviews on here give a reasonable portrait of the property. Nonetheless, there are a few things I'd like to point out that I think are important to booking a stay there.The good:- Grounds - The hotel is a lovely property. We found the room to be very spacious and very clean. A bit utilitarian (tile floors) but wise choices given the beach location. The beachfront itself is fantastic, some of the best in Puerto Rico. There are two pools which are very attractive. On both the beach and by the pools, there are always enough chairs.- Drinks - As others have noted, the bartenders make fantastic mojitos, pina coladas, and frozen mojitos. - Entertainment - Great tennis, golf, casino and lots of bars and restaurants. You certainly could have a pleasant vacation without leaving the grounds (though I would strongly advise going off grounds). The hotel can book virtually any activity for you (at their inflated prices, of course).- Family friendly - For those that have kids, it seems to be a great place for kids, but....The bad:- Kids - Obviously Easter weekend is the worst of the worst in terms of there being crowds and lots of families. The hotel does a great job of providing things for kids to do and it is a safe environment for them, generally, though we did see the hotel serving extremely young minors alcohol on one occasion. We stayed on the beach and away from the pool, where most of the kids were (even the quiet pool was full of screaming kids) so it did not bother us. They didn't make too much noise in the halls, though i could see that being an issue.- Service/Speed - I simply don't buy the concept of Caribbean time and as long as I am at an American-owned resort I consider extreme slowness and incompetence unacceptable. The hotel first tried to put us in an out-of-the-way room with two double beds until we complained and got the king we booked. Because the hotel is also the country club for wealthy locals, I repeatedly noticed that Puerto Rican locals were treated much better than out of town guests. The bartenders at the pool area were almost comically slow with drink service, to the point where other guests were yelling at them as they stood joking around, entering their tips into the computers, and otherwise not serving people. - Restaurants - The breakfast at Marbella was fairly good. We also had dinner at Aqualuna, the seafood place. It was pretty mediocre. Prices are basically on the higher end of New York prices, but the quality is not there - typical of a beach resort. Even for New Yorkers, we got some sticker shock when we saw that the Italian restaurant was charging nearly $30 for plates of pasta.There are several local places that are enjoyable, including Antojitos down the street. We also liked Las Vegas, just down the road, for dinner. We stayed here on Starwood points over a very busy weekend and were generally pleased with how the hotel handled the crowds. It was of course annoying that service was sometimes slow, and I was irked, though not surprised, at how much they nickel and dime you (nothing is complimentary, including in room internet). If you want an easy place to stay, it's a good place, and I note that on the following Monday (our last day) it got much quieter and more relaxing. Overall, not much about the place surprised me.

<Author>LimitedTraveler
<Content>Nice place to stay We stayed at the Westin with our kids (14/12) during Spring Break. Our room was clean, but it was a bit disappointing to walk the corridor to our room and see discarded room service left on the floor, sometimes for up to two days, without being taken away. It became a running joke with us to see when the trash would be picked up. I agree with most of the reviews about the staff and restaurants. The staff was friendly and accommodating, but service in most of the restaurants was slow. The food was fine. Although there are many restaurants on site, the menus in each are fairly limited. The pricing was about what you expect from a resort - very expensive. i could not believe they had the nerve to charge $45/person for Easter Brunch. We avoided that. The concierge staff was very friendly, but not as knowledgeable as I thought they should be. The beach was clean and we could always find a chair, even though the place was extremely crowded. The ocean at this location was very calm - no body surfing here. If you stay here and don't want to be stuck on the property, you have to rent a car. Don't rent a car at the hotel. When I called, they wanted to charge about $60/day for the smallest car. Instead, I rented a four-door at the airport for $200 for the week. The car came in very handy as we went to El Yunque (excellent), Hacienda Carabali (lots of fun for the kids) for horseback riding, Fajardo for the bioluminscent bay trip (a bit disappointing), and Old San Juan/El Morro (excellent). If you have a car, don't go through the concierge to arrange for these activities. They are extremely overpriced if you go through the hotel. Essentially, you are paying for the transportation. Plus, a car was necessary to go to Walmart (about 15 minutes away), Walgreens (about 10 minutes away), and the Belz Factory Outlet (about 15 minutes away). You need to stock up at these places rather than rely on eating at the hotel too often. But overall, this was a very good vacation spot.

<Content>Great Family Trip!!! I was so apprehensive based on the reviews here, but I am glad I went and BOY were they wrong!!!! This was a great hotel. Cons: as stated here a million times, this hotel is drastically understaffed, which makes no sense, especially in PR with an unemployment rate of 20%, There is little organization, and getting chairs by the pool on a holiday week required a serious plan of action- umbrellas were generally gone by 6:45 am (NOT kidding!) and more than 2 chairs together were gone by 8am,. Having primarily stayed in 4 or 5 star hotels, I went down to the pool the first day with a $20 in hand thinking I would pick my chairs...hahaha. They weren't even interested! The Casino is small(in comparision to the one at The Ritz) but adequate. They have a David's Cookies that has ice cream, cookies, desserts, and coffee. In the morning you can get coffee/ muffin for low cost breakfast. We mostly ate at the bar area which had a very nice delux continental breakfast for $15.00 including tax/gratuities. Thought this was a great deal and very good. Dinner at their main dinning room, Meres was very good. Lunch at Coqui was good-but do avoid dinner there. We ate twice at the Italian restaurant-Palio-which was very good. Service tends to be slower than what you would expect or hope for, but found that to be the tendency. I do have to say, though that the pleasant and accommodating staff made up for the slow service at times. We enjoyed our stay at the Westin and would return. Just need to know what you are looking for. Please email me with any questions.

<Author>luv2travel63
<Content>Had a great Vacation in Puerto Rico My wife and 2 daughters (12 and 15) just returned from a one week stay at the Westin. We were a little nervous staying at the Westin as the reviews are so mixed. Overall we had a great time and enjoyed the hotel. We were debating between the Caribe Hilton and the El Conquistador. We were very happy with our choice. We booked the hotelby calling the Westin and were given the lowest rate with AAA over the phone. It was 278 for ocean view per night plus taxes and resort fees. As mentioned earlier the resort fees are expensive so the room was about 340 per night with the extras. Yes the resort is remote so I would strongly recommend getting a car at the airport otherwise youare stuck on the property. We parked each night in the employee lot accross from the main lot and this was free otherwise parking was 15 per night.We booked one room for the four of us with two double beds and balcony. The room was clean and about average size. The view was toward the ocean but you really had to be on the balcony to see the ocean. We tried to upgrade as we are Starwood Gold but the hotel was overbooked and we could not move. I think we could have moved the next day but my kids were settled in so I did not try. The bedding was nice but the beds were not like the heavenly beds at other Westins. They were OK but not nearly as nice as the normal heavenly beds. The bathroom was nothing special with only one sink and tub shower combo with adequate hot water and water pressure. The housekeeping was fine and the room was kept clean each day. We did have a rollaway brought in as our kids don't like to sleep together so it was a little cramped and they also brought a small refrigeratorwhich was nice to keep beer and soda to take to the beach. There was no charge for the frig or the extra bed. The TV was 27 inches with an OK selection of channels but no movie channels. The Beach as the Westin was great. Large and clean with plenty of chairs and umbrellas. The waves were great and my 12 year old played for days with her boogie board. (we bought the boards at Walgreens for 9.99 and it was much cheaper than renting it from the hotel) The pools were also very nice but most of our time was at the beach. I believe there were activities at the pool but our kids did not do any of them. The workers at the Westin were all nice and helpful, except for the people handing out towels at the pool.We ate mostly at David's cookies for breakfast with scones and croissants. The prices were reasonable and OK food. We had buffet breakfast once at Meribels for about 23$ for adults and kids were half price. It was a little disappointing but the omeletes and bagels with lox were nice. The fruits were not good without any type of berries and a weak selection of pastries. We tried to leave the hotel for most of the dinner meals as the reviews of the hotel food had been so bad. We did eat at Shimas asian type food at the Westin and it was pretty bad and expensive (entres 27-38 and tea bag for $4.00). This convinced us to leave the hotel for dinners. Most of ourlunches were by the pool and the service and food was usually pretty good and prices were typical for carribean or hawaii. Entres and sandwiches between 11 and 15. Kids meals were $6 and were pretty good. For dinner we would try and leave the resort. We ate twice at La Perilla (or shack #2) at Loquilla beach about 10 minutes away. Itwas by far the best meal and a lot of fun. The people were very nice and great food (entres 17-30). I am a very snobby eater and I would highly recommend this place. We also ate Richies cafe which had a nice view but the food was not very good. One night we ate in San Juan at Dragonfly which was interesting food and fun but the music was a little too loud. Our other meal was in Fajardo at Isemar (sp) A very small fish place which was also pretty good and a lot of fun. You pick your own fish and they cook it for your. We stopped here after the bio bay tour.If you go to Puerto Rico do the Bio Bay tour in Fajardo. We used Las Tortugas tours [----] and our guide was Alvin. We booked on our own and it was 40$ per person (through hotel 75$). It was a lot of fun and highly recommend it. We explored the rain forest and hiked which was great as well. Overall we had a great time in Puerto Rico. The people were nice, great weather (no rain for the entire week), greatbeach and fun things to do. The Westin is not like the Four Seasons but is clean and has a nice pool and grounds. It's biggest weakness is the lack of good food options nearby or on property. San juan is about 40 minutes away and most of the nearby places are not very goodexcept for shack 2 at Loquilla. We were pleasantly surprised by the Westin and would return but do not expect ultra luxury from the hotel.David

<Author>deenaclaire
<Content>Okay. Just okay. We booked a package thru Orbitz, and it included a car rental, for which we were grateful. <Author>Vacation209
<Content>Great family vacation Our family of four (Mom, Dad and two teens) stayed at the Westin Rio Mar for six nights last week. It was our first time in Puerto Rico but not our first to the Caribbean-or to the Westin Caribbean resorts. We are Starwood Preferred members. Our flight landed at San Juan airport at 2:15 pm. We arrived at the hotel at 4pm-after renting a car at the airport. I would highly recommend renting a car as it came in very handy. The resort is in a remote area. Check in was fairly quick although a bit confusing as the clerk did not have the correct dates for our stay. We were shown to our room (a fairly large ocean front room overlooking the pool area/beach). The room was nicely arranged but not recently refurbished. The bed spread was dirty, the TV looked as though it had fallen one too many times but otherwise, I was impressed by the clean floor and room. We asked for fresh bedspreads and were immediately given them. We always had maid service before noon each day. We never heard anyone in the adjoining rooms but could hear noise from the hall.The hotel grounds are beautiful. The pool is a perfect temperature, uncrowded and very clean. We all loved the expansive beach and even liked the water with the waves. We were surprised by the lack of water sports offered at the beach (no parasailing, two jet skis, no banana boats,one sailboat) but not bothered by this at all. There were no vendors who came by while we were on the beach and this was nice. Umbrellas were available for free on a first come/first served basis. We did not have a drop of rain for six days although the rain clouds seem to hang over the rain forest. Be sure to tour the rain forest as it is a great but long hike. La Mina falls are beautiful.My one real problem with this hotel is the lack of food options, lack of food quality and expense. Count on $10 for any drink you order. We ate every morning at the David鈥檚 Cookies in the lobby where we got bagels, muffins and coffee. This was a bit hectic as the women working it were much more interested in talking amongst themselves than helping customers. Every day we ate lunch at Club Coqui beside the pool. It was expensive-about $90 for the four of us- and not very good. What it lacked in quality it made up for in convenience as we all wanted to enjoy the water and pool all day. We ate at the hotel three nights. Marabella鈥檚 was AWFUL. Iguana Pub was good and had the nicest view. We wanted to eat at Pailo but we did not have long pants so we couldn鈥檛. We had nice khaki shorts and nice collared shirts but we were told that shorts could not be worn. I think it is a silly rule for the Caribbean but no big deal. Off the resort, we ate at Antojitos, Brass Cactus and Don Pepes. All were just okay. From the outside, the restaurants all look sketchy, but once inside the food was, for the most part, acceptable. However, we were a little shocked to find a bunch of dogs on the roof of the building next to Don Pepe鈥檚. We wished we had found a nice restaurant but did not see any that fit that bill. Many other guests were complaining of the same problem as well and I feel that this issue is the main downfall for the hotel. The nearby towns of Luquillo and Fajardo are not very exciting and seemed poor and almost deserted to us. We enjoyed our trip but would probably not go back. This resort is very remote and I can鈥檛 imagine being without a car here. The hotel itself is nice but it could be a much more desirable property if the food options were improved.

<Author>hyelor
<Content>If you are looking to stay out of the city....... Our family of 4 (2 adults and 2 young adult kids) stayed here over Christmas break. Overall, it was a great experience. We are accustomed to traveling over popular vacation times, so we went with the understanding that the resort would be crowded, and boy was it crowded! But everyone who worked there did a pretty good job in keeping their cool despite some rude, obnoxious hotel guests. The hotel itself is beautiful and well located, if you are looking for a resort outside of the city. Access by the new superhighway is very easy and can take as little as 30 min., depending on the traffic. And there is a lot of traffic. Rent a car at the airport, as I heard that the hotel's car rental agency ran out of cars.The room was large enough for the 4 of us, and maid service as well as responses to special housekeeping requests were excellent. My husband is a Starwood Platiinum member, so we were lucky enough to stay on points, but we were not surprised that there was no upgrade available, even though they tried. Beware of the minibar- everytning in there, including water, is very expensive! Instead, go to a supermarket and stock up on essentials.All of the staff, in every part of the resort, were extremely polite and very nice to deal with. This goes especially for the concierges, who were helpful with restaurant suggestions and reservations. They have books of menus that you can browse through. We LOVED the Kiosk #2 (I think) in Luquillo, right off the highway. Fabulous food, and the owner/chef described every dish to us with such enthusiasm. On the other hand, stay away from the hotel food if at all possible. Very expensive and mediocre. So many superior options are available very close to the hotel. Do go to David's for morning coffee, and the beach bar for drinks while gazing at the ocean.If you are interested in side trips, the rain forest is a must. We took the hike down to the waterfall and it was worthwhile, but take extreme caution on the pavement as it is extremely slippery, even when wearing sneakers. (I slipped and fell and injured my foot, nothing serious but a nuisance to deal with while on vacation). Another must is kayaking on the bioluminescent bay, a unique experience- take a waterproof camera with a flash (very necessary) to document this awesome phenomenon. We did the rain forest on our own, but booked the kayaking through the concierge, and it was a little pricey but it included round trip transportation with a very nice driver. Old San Juan is a charming city with good restaurants and a lively street scene, an easy drive from the hotel.We stayed 5 nights and could easily have stayed longer. We would definitely return here!

Yes, food is expensive..breakfast buffet was $100 for 4..for breakfast!! so go to the davids cookies on property instead and get some bagels and muffins and lattes, bring them to the beach, and have a leisurely breakfast for a reasonable price, with your feet in the sand. tip: park in the employee lot across the street from the indoor lot , and get free parking. Overall, a most pleasant experience. try antonjiettes (spelling?) down the road for decent local food, in a friendly atmosphere, with very reasonable prices! and great mojitos! lastly, a rental car a must while staying at this property. enjoy.

HOTEL STRUCTURE- 4.5 stars- tasteful, rustic, lots of terra cottaearthtones. BALCONY was great, held a table with 2 chairs. great for having breakfast. BED was awesome, slept better than @ home. MAID SERVICE was there by 10:30 am every morning. ........ POOL- 4 stars- One of the thing I hate most about Vacations is getting up @ 7 am to get a poolside chaise w/ umbrella. The rio mar is no different. get there early for a choice spot. pool is nice, w/ a 4 leaf clover shape, big hot tub, fairly lame water slide for a hotel like this, kids seemed to like it though. seperate adult pool was very nice and fairly quiet..... BEACH-4 Stars- no powdery white or pink sand in Puerto Rico,Just nice soft brownish sand. beach must be a mile long and 50 yards wide, lots of chaises. fairly big waves, lots of fun for adults and kids. In my opinion 5 star staff abd service, prompt maid service a big plus...... THINGS TO DO:-5 -Stars- every hour they have different activities for those who don't like to sit. Hair braiding for kids, aqua robics, iguana feeding,kids bingo, P.M. bonfire w/ smores making, Poolside kids Movie at night. 2 golf courses, tennis, lots of excursions, they are pricey if you do through hotel(i rented a car(saved alot of money)..... OVERALL- Great family resort, not for a romantic getaway..... VALUE- While not cheap, I feel the hotel is priced right for what you get. P.S.-$70 resort fee is completely obnoxious, but i think most big resorts have this charge, it's a hoaxy charge, all the stuff you think is free is really not(complimentary room coffee,beach towels,shampoo,shuttle service,plus any thing else you think is complimentary is paid for for via the resort fee.) I Will be going back, overall great experience, but manage your expectations. Go for a family vacation, not for the food.

<Author>tosha25italia
<Content>Shady Scene We arrived at 4am and check in took about 20 minutes. First they did not have us arriving until the next day, until we had a paper copy of the confirmation. It seemed like a ploy. We planned the vacation as a romantic getaway weekend, and as such, reserved a king size bed with ocean view. After the long and slow check in process, we were sent to our room and surprised to see 2 double beds. We went back to the desk and were told there were no king size beds left, and we would have to wait until the morning. We went back to our room and realized the ocean view was really a view of the trees and pool with the ocean in the background, hardly an ocean view. The next morning we went to the front desk and were jerked around, told we were still on the waiting list. Later on that day found out that there were 20 % king bed rooms and 80% double. Also that there was no availability. Needless to say we spent the weekend in double beds. This was not a huge thing, but only the beginning of our experience at the Rio Del Mar.  The service in the Marbella Restaurant was awful. We went for breakfast and had to obtain our own menus because we were waiting so long. For lunch, it took 40 minutes for our order to arrive- they were waiting for the pizza to cook. Each day, a new miscellaneous charge appeared on our bill, whether we were double charged for lunch or charged for the mini bar which we did not use. The front desk was condescending if anything, unhelpful and unable to provide the service that most people expect. It was unacceptable. The food in the Grille Room could be compared to Outback Steakhouse but 3 times the cost.  The day BEFORE we were to check out, we received our bill under the door. We had to again go to the front desk who claimed we were checking out that day, but again, provided them with the paper confirmation to show that we were checking out the next day. Later that day, our room key did not work, because even though we had fixed the problem, they did not fix it in the system. As far as the noise, you can hear the people above you moving things around, and if they are using the shower, you will know it. Don't use the shower at the same time as anyone else in the hotel, or you will lose pressure. Overall, the service was terrible, and we felt that we were being scammed each day.I would NEVER return there. If I had to, I would lower my expectations of food or bring my own.

<Author>jdmPA
<Content>Great vacation for the whole family! We recently spent 5 days at the Westin Rio Mar with our 3 young children. Everyone had a fantastic time - the resort is beautiful, the staff was wonderful and the weather was perfect. I was a bit concerned after reading some of the reviews, but all of our expectations were met or exceeded! We would definitely return to this resort for our next vacation.Some specific points:1) The staff throughout the hotel was wonderful, helpful and friendly. Frances and Shelly, the pool activity coordinators were super - my kids loved the hair braiding, iguana feeding, sand castle building and bingo. 2) Food is expensive at the resort restaurants - Davids Cookies is good for breakfast (bagels, muffins, coffee). We rented a car and checked out the local restaurants for dinner (Don Pepe's, La Parilla, Lolittas and Metropol were all very good). There are grocery stores within 10 minutes of the resort. Walmart is 15 minutes away. 3) Driving is very scary, especially during peak times, lots of traffic, motorcycles spliiting lanes, drivers not stopping at intersections, etc. Be very careful!!4) The beach at the resort is beautiful - aqua blue water, soft brown sand, lots of sand dollars and shells. The waves are great for bodysurfing, but the undertow is strong (be careful with small children - there is no lifeguard at the beach)5) Pools are clean, well maintained and the kids enjoyed the waterslide at the activity pool. Food and drink service is available at both pools (drinks are expensive). We had no issues with overcrowding at the pool although toward the end of our week, more people were coming into the resort (for Presidents weekend). All in all it was a great week!

<Author>jp16
<Content>good time as usual I am in Puerto Rico 4-5 times per year and stay at the Westin at least once per year. I have read a lot of reviews on the hotel and perhaps I can shed some light....First of all, the hotel has over 600 rooms so what you read here is a very small sample of opinions, some helpful and some obviously reactionary. I can comment on a few things I have seen. First, the area is plenty safe. I am not sure why people think it is unsafe other than just a simple fear of being around people that are different than you or perhaps a bad experience which you could have anywhere. Second, there is a ton to do in the area. If you couldn't find it you didn't ask because people are very friendly when you show them some respect as oppossed to acting like they are your servants...any of us who have been to any resort know what I am talking about. Anyway, some recommendations for things to do would be renting ATV's or going horseback riding right off the Westin grounds up into the mountains near El Yunque. There is a cool bar at the top of the mountains to hang out and relax in. You can make a short trip to fajardo and go to one of the marina's where you can take catamaran trips that provide you with snorkeling gear and take you out to the reefs off the small islands just east of PR. They provide rum drinks and food and are all included in the price. You can also go deep sea fishing or just take the ferry to Culebra or Vieques at 2.25 per person. The bio-bay's in Fajardo and Vieques are a once in a lifetime must do's. Very Surreal and the tours leave nightly. You can hike in El Yunque, the Caribbean National Rainforest as well. As far as restaurants go there are plenty of good ones off the Westin campus as well. Let me give you a hint though....If you are looking for steak and cheese or a pizza you're better off having it at home. The good food is what people are used to making and in Puerto Rico the seafood is excellent and some local dishes such as Mofongo and Asopao are really awesome. You can go to Don Pepe which serves Mexican and Island food. Hint: you are not in Mexico so what shouldn't you order? La Parilla is a seafood shack in the kiosks, number 2 which has good seafood. If you prefer a restaraunt make a trip to Fajardo and eat at Rosa's or Irbella for fresh off the boat seafood. Don't expect Legal Seafood decor as these places are very rustic, but good and in most cases the food is at least as good as the seafood where I am from(Boston). On the Westin campus the food is expensive and pretty typical of resort food which is good but over-priced. I think the combo leaves some people upset and rightfully so. The Italian restaurant is the best one of the lot at the Westin. The grill room has decent burgers and sandwiches but if that is what you want go off campus to Luquillo to a place called the Brass Cactus. Finally, if swanky dining is what you want go to San Juan where there are many more modern choices. In my opinion Dragon Fly is the best of them in old San Juan. It is an Asian fusion restaurant that blends local ingredients into food with Asian flare. There is a ceviche bar owned by the same person next to it called Aguaviva. Authentic Puerto Rican is best at Ajili Mojili and I happen to like the Asopao at Barrachina which is a great lunch spot in old San Juan with courtyard seating. A couple of things to perpare yourself for:1. The driving on the island is a little scary so be careful. It's best to drive later at night to avoid traffic or mid-day.2. You are on island time down there so the service can be a little slow...embrace it because the reality is you are probably there to unwind and relax from the crazy hectic life you already live.3. Treat people well, especially the bartenders and they will give you the shirt off their backs. All you have to do is read some of the malicious reviews here and you'll understand what they are dealing with.Finally, the Westin isn't perfect. There are other places that offer different things both in PR and on the other islands. But the beach is nice and relaxing, they treat families well and there is a whole island to explore if you so choose. Have fun, I always do.

<Author>njr
<Content>Westin Rio Mar - Average at Best My husband and I recently returned from a 1 week stay at Westin Rio Mar. My husband had a 4 day conference and we stayed on for 3 vacation days. Because it was for a conference, we didn't have a choice in staying there. Based on reviews here, the location and the amenities offered, I honestly would not have selected this resort and after a 1 week stay, I would not recommend this resort to others.First things first, many people have stated and people still seem to be surprised so I will repeat it, the resort is a 30 minute drive from San Juan and it can take up to 1 hour if there is traffic. If you don't rent a car, you will be stuck at the resort and subject to poor service and average, overpriced food. The positives:- I found the concierge helpful, particularly with off-site restaurant recommendations, the common areas of the resort are nice and I enjoyed the quiet pool. The gym has decent equipment and the preplaced towel and water bottle at each machine is a nice touch. Staff in the gym and spa were helpful and attentive. I had a swedish massage and thought it was great. While I wasn't particularly impressed with the beach, others in our group did enjoy it. It was particularly windy while we were there and the red flags, indicating rough/dangerous water, were up most of the time. The negatives- maybe I haven't noticed this at other resorts- but the $39/day resort service fee seemed a bit steep, particularly when you still have to pay for golf, tennis, spa treatments and excursions as well as the $30 room tax . We did not have a problem getting reservations the 2 times we ate dinner at Palio's and Aqualuna. We thought the food was average and the pricing was okay at these restaurants. Service was slow and not particulary attentive. Service was particulary bad/slow/inattentive and I did have a problem with food quality, selection and pricing at Marbella and Club Coqui. Marbella's is the restaurant that serves breakfast and the staff really push the buffet, which I found to be average. The a la carte menu has a decent selection of standard breakfast items- but seriously, $6.00 for a small bowl of oatmeal?? $4.00 for 1 Dannon yogurt?? $5.50 for a bowl of Cornflakes?? We had to repeatedly ask for drinks It was not unusual to wait at least an hour for our food to be served after we had ordered at Coqui or by the pool. I was willing to overlook the negatives listed above, until the real negative emerged. The one that still grosses me out and was the absolute deal breaker for me is that there are in fact bed bugs. I had read about this in advance, but did not believe until several people in our group had to be moved to other rooms and the hotel began to exterminate. Unfortunately, on the last morning of our trip, my husband and I both woke up covered in bites. I've never had this happenTwo years ago, I stayed at the Wyndham El Conquistador, which is about 20 minutes further on Rt.3. It was it's drawbacks- it's huge, requires a funicular to get to different areas of the resort and the beach is a ferry ride away, but I wouldrecommend the El Conquistador over the Westin for sure.

<Author>reddyn
<Content>expensive and not so safe. We just came back from a conference in PR. Many people stayed at the hotel, some at the Villas which are considered separate from the hotel. I told the manager about the incident, but the days following, I noticed that the lifeguards showed little interest in watching the water. <Author>travelbugs5
<Content>A Happy New Year at the Rio Mar I have to preface this review by saying I might be a bit more critical had I been paying $800 per night for my room! As it was we paid half that for one day (coupon) and the other nights were on Starwood points, so we didn't have too much to complain about from the get go. The Westin Rio Mar is set on a beautiful beach northeast of San Juan. The property is lovely, and the landscape is beautiful. I never grew tired of looking at a lagoon pool with palm trees and a stretch of beach in the background! The staff was friendly, and efficiency kind of depended on the luck of the draw. I agree Caribbean time is very laaaaaaaaiiiiddddddd baaaaaccccckkkkkk! If you're in a hurry, go to a large bustling city. We wanted to leave that behind so the big slowdown was not a problem. Our worst service was at a local restaurant that was highly recommended on this website (La Parilla). We waited over an hour for our food! But I have to say, it was worth the wait...more flavorful and a much better value than anything we ate at the hotel. You really must rent a car if you go to this property. It made all the difference for us. For one thing, it sounds like (and was the case for us) most of the restaurants go on some kind of hiatus throughout the year. There were a mere 5 restaurants open during the busy New Year's week. That's out of 12! Oh, but David's Cookies was a lifesaver, with bagels in the morning and ice cream at night....I would imagine that's a staple there, and doesn't close seasonally. We ate at Shimas. It was pretty good. I would say our sushi at home is much better but they had a dessert that was the best thing we ate in Puerto Rico....a banana crepe with vanilla/macadamia nut ice cream. Maybe skip the sushi, get their entree, and GET DESSERT THERE! Marbella is a restaurant right off the lobby serving your basic family fare. A salad was $14 to $16 and sparse to say the least. As you might expect from a resort hotel, you will pay up on food and drinks. Tropical drinks poolside are $9 so plan ahead to pay up because they are frozen and fabulous and you can order from your chaise on the beach, at the pool or in the hot tub. It's quite the treat! The Club Coqui, the restaurant that's poolside was a huge ripoff. We paid $82 for lunch there one day for the five of us...and not for any feast, either! The trouble is, there aren't a lot of options for lunch and we wanted to stay on the grounds. So in a sense, they've gotcha! Definitely hit the bakery at the corner of Rt. 3 where you turn in for the resort. They have great sandwiches and are super friendly there. Wish we had discovered that earlier in the trip. Seeing the rainforest on our own was great. It's very close to the resort. I don't think I would have wanted to pay the hotel tour fee times five. We did fine on our own and hiked to the waterfall--gorgeous. The path was clearly marked. It WAS NOT muggy and buggy like I'd imagined, but cool and comfy. But wear gym shoes! Leave plenty of time for Old San Juan. We cut it too close to our return flight, ran into traffic, and had a hard time parking, which was disappointing because it looked really fun. Plan a half day at least for Old San Juan. But the thing is, you'll find it hard to leave this nice resort. We loved the climate, too, where you never broke a sweat, but were always comfy and warm. Shade was plentiful so staying outside all day between the pool and beach was no problem. The lounge chairs at the quiet pool are especially nice and if you have a great book, you may never want to leave!One funny thing...I was disappointed that our ocean front view (which is extra $$ as well as higher points) was blocked by a huge palm tree. We decided to live with it, but the third day they trimmed all of the palm trees and our view improved 100%. You'd think we had requested that! It was like night and day and the latter part of the week we felt we had the best view in the place.We really enjoyed our stay. No, this Westin wasn't a perfectly oiled machine like some we've stayed at. We travel a lot, but critique our vacations by how much fun we have as a family. We were so happy to be away and in a warm climate that I think nothing bothered us too much. We had a blast. I recommend it for pure relaxation and family time.

<Author>butter
<Content>Just back from the Westin Rio Mar.... We just got back from a long weekend at the Westin Rio Mar. There had been some mixed reviews here, so I was ready to see for myself. Overall we had a great time. I'll caveat that by saying we got upgraded to a huge suite, which of course made the trip even better. Not sure how big the standard rooms are. The staff who checked us in did a great job and were very nice. The staff at the poolside were not as good, and one time I placed a beverage order which never showed up so I went to the poolside bar myself to get it. It wasn't a big deal, but that's not great service. There are 2 pools + a kiddy pool. The first day we sat at the adult quiet pool but then the other days we sat by the activity pool. Even though we liked the quiet of the adult pool, the activity pool got more sun. We had no problem getting seats by the pool. In terms of food, our package included breakfast, which is served buffet style and had made-to-order omelets as well as many other selections. The hotel restaurants are average for dinner. Expensive and mediocre (but not terrible) food. We ate at The Grille Room, Palio and Shimas and I'd say you can skip Shimas. We also ate one night off campus at Don Pepe, a local restaurant recommended by the concierge, and it was terrific! Go there! We enjoyed the spa. They were always running late, but you atill got the full-time of your service.We didn't bring our kids, but it seems to be a very kid-friendly place.... it was packed with families. The casino is small but on a busy night, it did open up some additional blackjack tables. We chose the Westin over the Ritz Carlton mostly because the Ritz Carlton rooms do not all have balconies, and I love to read outside on the balcony in the AM while my husband sleeps late. I ddin't price out the Ritz this time, but my guess is that the Westin is also more reasonably priced. There is the downside of it being further from the airport, but that only took about 45 minutes and I don't feel like I lost out on so much time because of it.Overall, I would go back again, especially if with my kids.

<Author>wromig
<Content>Overall - Very Nice My wife and I returned from a week's stay at the Westin. First of all, we found the grounds and the pool area to be beautiful. We enjoyed having an adults only pool and the ocean was wonderful. Our room was clean and very nice. We have been to many different resorts in the Caribbean and this is certainly one of the nicest. For the most part, the staff is courteous and pleasant. We found the bartenders at the Tiki Bar, the wait staff in all of the restaurants and the maids to be polite and friendly. Ivan and Victor at the Tiki Bar were terrific to us. We found the Assistant Restaurant Manager, who was from Sardinia (I feel badly that I cannot remember his name but the Westin should give him a raise and make sure he does not leave), to be absolutely wonderful and professional. When we checked in, we inquired about getting a room on a higher floor and she began searching on the computer for one. In the meantime, she asked us if we would like copies made of our transfer vouchers. I said yes and she took off to make the copies. 15 minutes later she returned while a line developed behind us. Her only comment was that the delay was because my wife asked for a higher room. We were both steamed over that incident. Next, we went to the concierge desk to sign up for tours. Please note if they do not get enough people, you do not get to go, although you have to hang around to find out if the tours will be cancelled or not. Two of ours were and on another one the wrong date was written down. In the future, I think it is best to rent a car although the fee for parking the car at the resort is exhorbitant. I do not even have enough time to go through the aggravation that my wife was put through to buy post card stamps. Some advice to the hotel would be sell post card stamps in the gift shop where you sell the cards. Also, do not have a policy for some parts of the hotel where you are forbidden to pay cash (the Tiki Bar for example) and other parts of the hotel (the concierge desk) where you have to pay cash for items like post card stamps. It's stupid things like that which keep this from being just an outstanding hotel. As for the restaurants, they are certainly resort high. We found the Grill Room to be a rip-off. My $40 steak was good but not great, and my wife's salmon was horrible for $28. On the other hand, we found Palio to be wonderful and the Japanese restaurant (which is not open all that often) to be good. We enjoyed eating off-site at nearby Don Pepe's where the food was good and the staff wonderful. A $14 shuttle from the hotel gets you there but it's worth it. Even though we did not get to eat there, we heard from others that the food at the restaurant at the main turnoff to the hotel from Rte. 3 was also very good. El Yunque was fun, I loved swimming in the waterfall and our guide was terrific. Old San Juan (we rented a car for the day from Avis at the hotel) was special to see also. I hate to be so negative about some things because overall we loved the hotel and would certainly come back, but we would rent a car and avoid the concierge desk at all costs.

<Author>KH8th

<Author>WillieC
<Content>Very Nice Hotel in Great Location We spent one night pre-cruise at the Westin Rio Mar. We rented a car from Hertz at the San Juan airport and drove to the Westin. Here is a tip: the Hertz trip computers at the desk will route you to the Westin via Route 23 (I think that is it), but Route 66 is MUCH faster. 23 is a busy street with stop light on almost every corner while 66 appears to be just recently opened and is more of a freeway with at least one toll booth ($1.50). However using 66 will save you at least 15-20 minutes I think. If using Hertz ask the front desk people about 66 - if you don鈥檛 they just wave you over to the computer terminal to print out the map. Other companies may tell you about 66 on their maps.Back to the hotel. I am surprised by some of the negative reviews posted here. We found the hotel to be quite nice, with beautiful grounds, great pools and hot tubs, and a very, very nice beach. The public areas were extremely nice and our room was large and roomy and of course had the Westin Heavenly Bed. The bathroom was large, there was adequate closet and storage space, an in room safe, and coffee and tea equipment and supplies. The room was spotless in every respect. Every staff member we dealt with was polite and helpful. As we wanted to visit El Yunque (just a few minutes away) the morning before we checked out to return to San Juan to board our cruise ship I enquired about a later check out time than the normal noon. They gladly extended the check out time to 3 pm which was ideal for us, giving us time to shower and clean up before returning to San Juan. That was very generous of them.We did not eat in any of the dining areas but did use the David Cookies for bagels and cream cheese in the morning. Things at David were priced reasonably. The posted menus at the various dining venues indicated that the prices were typical for a big hotel/resort. We had dinner at a small local place just outside the gate down the road before reaching the main highway. The food was excellent, the owner was extremely friendly and the prices were reasonable. This was Antojitos Puertorrique帽osCarr. 968 #160, Bo. Las ColesRio Grande, PR 00745 (787) 888-7378Puerto Rican FoodWe visited El Yunque the morning prior to returning to San Juan and it was extremely interesting. There are several places where one can hike into the forest and see waterfalls, the trees, etc, or one can just drive around, pulling off at vista points here and there. Either way it is well worth seeing. One hint 鈥?get there early. Since we were staying close we were there before 9am. Before we left (about noon) the place was packed with tour busses, probably from San Juan and cruise ships. We returned to the Westin, showered, packed, checked out and returned to San Juan to turn in the car and board the cruise ship. Here is another big hint. We reserved the car for airport pickup and downtown San Juan return to the Hertz office. We had a difficult and frustrating time finding the downtown office, and since we drove right past the airport to get downtown it seemed that maybe an airport turn in would have been better. However, unless Hertz offers courtesy shuttles from the airport to the docks then a cab ride would have been needed. The downtown office did provide free transfers to the cruise dock.Overall we would rate the Westin Rio Mar highly and would stay there again. We found it to be much more relaxing than staying in San Juan and being able to see El Yunque easily was a real plus. One thing to note is that the parking is not included and the rate is $15 a day for self parking - a bit of a rip but not much you can do about it.

<Content>Great Resort - Can NOT understand the negative reviews!! This resort was fabulous, we were there for 5 nights and had a great time. Most complain that it is far away from San Juan, that they needed to rent a car, that the food was expensive, etc.So what? The location is right near the rainforest in a beautiful location. It is about a 30-45 minute drive from San Juan, depending on traffic. The beach is a beautiful beach, no, it is not the white sand, crystal clear turqouise water of the Caribbean, but that is because it is located on the Atlantic side of the ocean. Duh. Look at a map and look at the pictures of the resort before you book the trip there!!The rooms were great. The standard room is large, with a nice sitting area. It was very clean, I have no idea what a previous poster was talking about dirty rooms. We were upgraded to a junior suite after one night (once the hotel cleared out a convention, and with a $20 tip to the reception - TIP - in ANY hotel, if you want to be upgraded to a better room, be prepared to tip the person who can put you in that better room!) and it was beautiful. But even the standard room was great.We didn't really eat in the hotel's restaurants because we were on the go so much. We did eat at the coffee place next to the casino every morning, which was a good, cheap alternative to spending a lot of money on the hotel food. I did check out the food prices and thery did not seem any higher than at any other Westin, and in fact, I thought the room serive prices were quite reasonable for a large hotel (I have seen double the prices charged at other hotels). We did order room service one night and it was quick and good food. Also, rent a car and explore the restaurants around the resort, there are plenty - I highly recommend Kiosk #2 at Loquillo beach, very close to the resort.The service at the hotel is fabulous - we wanted a fridge for our room, and one was there within 10 minutes. The safe didn't work in out first room (the person prior to us didn't leave it open), and someone was there in a matter of minutes to fix it. My husband got food poisioning, and the concierge helped out immensly, getting a dr to our room immediately, and even sending someone to go get the prescription from a local pharmacy. The staff could not have done more, they are truly great and extremly friendly and care about their jobs and their customers.Overall we had a great time at the Westin and would not hesitate to return or recommend it for a great vacation. Don't listen to the whiners and complainers - honestly, if they didn't like this hotel, I cannot imagine that any hotel would live up to their expectations (I have traveled all over the world and stayed at numerous 5 star resorts - the Westin Rio Mar lived up to its 4 star rating)Here's another tip - you can book this hotel through Hotwire or Priceline for a substantial savings, which makes it an even better deal.

<Author>jrnyman6
<Content>Great Vacation at the Rio Mar My wife and I visited Puerto Rico from August 16-21. We chose the Rio Mar for its amenities and we were not disappointed. Through research on this website, we also knew what to expect (distance from San Juan) which for us was perfect. Our only complaint was that most of the resort's restaurants were closed sporadically through our stay. We ventured off the property for dinner twice and quickly learned our lesson. You're much better off eating at the Westin or making the trek all the way to San Juan.We were upgraded to a suite without even asking (I had booked a resort view room online) and it was very spacious. The bed, as advertised, was extremely comfortable. Everything was clean and new.The hotel's beach is well maintained. There are thatched umbrella stands for those who need some shade, and also portable umbrellas that the staff will set up for you. Just get there early because they seemed to run out every day. If you're a golfer, be sure to check out the two Rio Mar courses. They are both high-quality and reasonably priced. Plus, there are iguanas everywhere.Driving in Puerto Rico is a little hectic. People either drive way too fast or way too slow...not a good combination. On top of that, most people are recklessly impatient. Not too different from NYC...except with palm trees on the side of the road.Overall we had a great experience in Puerto Rico. We found the people to be friendly, the weather was terrific, and the Rio Mar lived up to its billing. We would definitely go back.

<Author>sedona74
<Content>Please read this: Terrible!!! INTRO: Starwood Hotels owns Westin, Sheraton, and the W hotels (our favorite). We are Starwood Preferred Guests and have had wonderful experiences at some of these hotels; my husband works in the travel industry. We are not snobs, nor are we wealthy people, but our experience at the Westin Rio Mar was...terrible. We've all read terrible reviews of hotels on these sites. We read things like air conditioning broken or smelly room or rude staff. I always take these with a grain of salt; I tend to think they are either phony reviews, or just written by incredibly picky people who are never happy with anything. This review, I promise you, is neither. ROOM: At first, they tried to give us a first floor room next to the pool, but I requested something higher up. So we were given a room at the back of the hotel, overlooking the ramp where the trucks and buses come in. The tiled floor hadn't been vacuumed; it had long black hairs, crumbs (dry oatmeal?), and dust. The rooms feel cold and wet. At night, the sheets feel like cold wet noodles around your body, and one night after they changed them, they actually stunk of feet, bleach, and mildew. After complaining (about a lot more than just the room), they did give us an ocean-view room on the 6th floor, but the only thing different was the view. This time it was the area rug that hadn鈥檛 been vacuumed; you could see white and yellow crumbs against the brown carpet. The coffee  tea bags next to the coffee-maker were torn open. There is no mini-fridge to keep cold water or leftover food from the restaurants.RESTAURANTS: Appalling. Out of 12 restaurants advertised (half are pool/pub food, and the other half fine dining), only 3 were actually open. There was no indication of this when we booked, or when we arrived. After winding our way on foot in the dark, through abandoned, un-lit paths, looking for the only Puerto Rican restaurant on the resort (it was labeled 鈥渦pscale鈥?, past abandoned lots with parked trucks and not one other human for 20 minutes, we found a boarded-up restaurant. Disappointed and in disbelief, we walked back to the hotel. The Sushi place was also closed. The steakhouse was somewhere out on the golf course, but we didn鈥檛 want to keep searching in the dark for another restaurant. (No one told us about the shuttle until our last day.) There was an Italian place, but we didn鈥檛 travel from New York to Puerto Rico to eat Italian food. The only other thing left was the hotel dining room, Marbella, billed as casual/family fare. People wore tank tops, shorts, and flip-flops, and parked baby strollers near their tables. We sat for 20 minutes and no one came to take our order. We got up and left for the Italian place, our last resort, but they wouldn鈥檛 allow us in because of my husband鈥檚 dressy dark jeans, which he paired with a crisp button-down and shiny black dress shoes. The restaurant only had a few tables full. Although we鈥檇 just walked 40 minutes in the dark, only to find closed up restaurants, they had no sympathy. Since the website pictures make it look like a young, trendy, hip hotel with a nightlife and many different types of dining options, my husband did not bring 鈥渟lacks.鈥?We complained to the concierge, who gave us a print-out of the only 3 restaurants open at the resort: the dining room, the Italian place and the steakhouse out on the golf course鈥攁nd the last two didn鈥檛 allow jeans! All she could do was escort us back down to the dining room, and give us a complimentary meal (only she kept saying it like it was coming out of her own pocket and expected us to be grateful). She began speaking Spanish to the maitre-d, I guess explaining the situation, but being that the staff is supposed to speak English, it was very disrespectful not knowing what they were saying about us. Thankfully, there were two or three Latin-influenced dishes on the menu, and they were very tasty. Had that not been the case, we would have left the next day. On our last day, we decided to have lunch in the dining room before our shuttle left for the airport. But they were not serving any meals because of a convention buffet. When we asked the concierge about it, she told me that being a Friday, it was going to be pretty hard to find a place to eat lunch.STAFF: Generally slow  annoyed that you are there. Waiters/waitresses slowly pad and saunter around the restaurants or grounds, the way I pad around my kitchen on a Sunday morning with my coffee. When walking around the pool/beach areas with their trays, they actually turn their heads when you try to make eye contact. We weren't served once while sitting by the pool or beach, although we would have loved to be. At the dining room, Marbella, the waiter never came to take our order, and just left us sitting there. This happened on two different nights. One morning at the breakfast buffet, I waited patiently for someone to come over to the omelette station and make me an omelette. Finally when the cook slowly sauntered out from the back, she just sighed and stared at me as if I were interrupting her day of relaxation. When she finished making my omelette of orange artificial egg mixture, she put a large handful of cold shredded cheese on it, and looked away over her shoulder to talk to someone while folding it over and onto my plate. Of course the omelette opened right back up again like a raw pizza, and I had to stand there and press it down myself with a clean plate, trying desperately to melt the cold cheese. The best part? Other staff members see you struggling with something or being ignored, and they just look away and continue talking with each other in clusters. Finally, on our last day while waiting for our shuttle to take us to the airport, I asked the head bellman whether the shuttle that was sitting out front was going to the airport, or to the golf course. He said to the golf course. But a minute later, the bus driver jumped off the bus and began loading luggage into the back of it. When we asked the driver about it, he said it was in fact going to the airport. I guess the bellman didn't care whether I made it home. He just wanted to shut me up, a very common attitude at this hotel.BEACH: We were told the ocean was both Atlantic and Carribean combined. This was not true; the beach was no different from any Atlantic beach, similar to Miami: crashing waves swirling with brown cloudy sand. The lounge chairs are made of hard wicker and are extremely uncomfortable, leaving marks on your skin even when covered with two towels. While drifting to sleep listening to the ocean waves, staff circle you in noisy trucks that stink of exhaust, picking up any empty chairs, no matter how close they are to where you鈥檙e lying, and piling them toward the back of the beach. Also, loud electric weed trimmers disturb your peaceful relaxation. The smell of gasoline permeates the air. I guess they were trying to get a head start on cleaning up so they could go home early? POOL: There are two pools: the larger, family pool, and the smaller Quiet Pool with waterfall. Despite the gigantic sign (in both Spanish and English) clearly indicating the rules (No horseplay, No children under 12 without adult, No running, etc.) the Quiet Pool was filled with young children and teenagers loudly playing around, tackling, throwing balls hard at each other, running, climbing, and doing somersaults off the waterfall. No one--parents, staff, etc.--seemed to notice or care. GUESTS: The majority of guests are either locals, or Puerto Ricans from New York. During the day, the pools and ocean were somewhat full, but at night, we would take walks outside or through the hotel, and we just wouldn鈥檛 see any other people. It felt lonely and sad being the only ones sitting on the veranda having drinks. We wondered where all the guests were. It was eerie.REGION: The stretch between San Juan and the 鈥渢own鈥?of Rio Grande is littered with decaying shacks and, ironically, brand new strip malls stuffed with KFCs, Subways, and Burger Kings鈥ll alongside an obnoxious 4-lane highway jammed with traffic, connecting to a new 6-lane interstate. You can reach the El Yunque Rainforest after driving through an impoverished, decaying neighborhood, but we couldn鈥檛 find any trails or waterfalls or places to pull off and explore.TIME OF YEAR: They say that it was off-season when we went; we couldn鈥檛 understand why. We had asked a friend who is from the Dominican Republic whether July/August was an okay time to go. She said (and our research confirmed) that hurricane season is actually May鈥擮ctober, and plenty of people vacation to the Carribean in summer. The weather was gorgeous: balmy, low-to-mid 80s, and mostly sunny. We didn鈥檛 understand how this could be a factor in any of the things we experienced. <Author>tomsak
<Content>Don't hesitate for a nice vacation here Just returned from 4 days at the Westin Rio Mar. Family of 4, girls 10 and 12. It was a wonderful stay. I would like to second the sentiment of an earlier poster from NJ about some people having to complain about everything. There is very little to complain about regarding the things that this resort can control. The weather is obviously one (Fortunately, it was beautiful. Yes, the rain showers come and go but that is what the Caribbean is, especially in the summer. This eastern end of the island is definitely cooler than San Juan or Dorado). The preponderance of locals is another (A hotel is a fixed asset. They have 600 rooms to fill. Since it is the slow season for American tourists to visit, they do run deals for the locals and they do come, especially on the weekends. Gee, imagine that, Puerto Ricans like to go on vacation too and have enough money to do so鈥ood for them. When tourists come to NYC, do they complain about all the local New Yorkers? Maybe, but that鈥檚 the way it is. In the summer, I believe Americans will be in the minority at this resort. So what. If you want everyone to be like you, go to the socioeconomic targeted Disneyworld resort hotel of your choice. There were a few instances of loud and uncontrolled behavior by the local kids. This was, however, no worse than that exhibited by some spoiled American brats, a scene which unfortunately has become commonplace at many high end resorts.)Rooms 鈥?Nice, large, clean, well-furnished in crisp Caribbean style. Heavenly beds were very comfortable. Nice size balconies, received a direct oceanfront upgrade by just asking upon check-in. No bed bugs. I agree with others that the bites, especially on kids, are a function of the tiny flies on the beach. They seemed to be present only at dusk. We did not go on the beach at night. Use bug repellent or just go from pool to ocean and back without lounging there. As you may read, bed bugs are becoming more of a problem worldwide, even at the Ritz-Carlton and Four Seasons. Learn how to check before you settle in and unpack.Grounds 鈥?Very nice, well-kept. Pools are clean and large. The 鈥渜uiet鈥?pool has somewhat tired loungers with mats but for heaven鈥檚 sake, put a towel over them. The larger 鈥渁ctivity鈥?pool has new loungers that are much nicer than the typical white strapped vinyl variety. Pool service, beach bar, live music, activities such as aquatic aerobics, bingo, free hair braiding for the kids. And the Westin Kids Club, always a good thing. The beach is beautiful, soft sand, mild waves, warm water, clean, lifeguard on duty every day. Not many resorts bother with lifeguards anymore, even Hawaii. So the sand is tan and not white鈥s there a problem with that?Restaurants 鈥?What you would expect at a large resort. Basically average, occasionally great and sometimes disappointing. Always expensive compared to eating out off campus. But overall it was fine.Service 鈥?Every single employee was helpful, upbeat, friendly, respectful and quick with a smile. Very rare anywhere today.Go, have a good time. Try to get a deal like the Escape package (we paid $209 with breakfast included for 2, all taxes, fees, tips included). If you overpay, then I guess you will always find something to complain about.

<Author>marchb4
<Content>Great time at the Westin Rio Mar! So we all know how much we like reading the reviews in Trip Advisor about the places we are planning to visit on vacation, hoping to figure out the best place stay, eat, etc. Well, we just got back from a 6-night stay at the Westin Rio Mar and would highly recommend it! We traveled from San Juan in a rental car. We chose Alamo - low prices, convinient to airport, and we were in and out in less than 10 minutes. Make sure to take the new toll road, Highway 66, from San Juan to just outside Rio Grande, that cuts your travel time by about 20-25 minutes. It only costs $1.50 and is really worth it as an alternative to the congested Route 3. It is so new that you won't find it on most maps yet.We arrived at the Westin in the late afternoon and were upgraded (without asking) to an oceanview room. Summer is the off season and there may be more flexibility. ROOM: Average size, attractive furniture, great beds, spotless, quiet POOLS/BEACH:There are two pools, one is the quiet pool with CUSHIONED lounge chairs, our choice. The beach is adjacent and great for boogie boarding. There are cabana for rent at $90 per day (comes with sodas, fruit, chips and ice chest). We just went down by 9ish and picked our spot under an umbrella. (Discounted with the Escape Package - see below) RESTAURANTS: The nice restaurants are somewhat expensive ($25-40 per entree) so we ate local cafes (for authentic Puerto Rican food) including Don Pepe's, Restaurante Terraza Montemar, and in San Juan. The Marbella in the Westin, has a morning full b-fast buffet ($19) but you can also order off the menu. It is also open for dinner with fair prices. TIP: We reserved the Escape Package online for which included 2 free b-fast buffets each day, 25% discount on all services, and included the resort/room tax which comes to almost 25% more. We would highly recommend this option if you can reserve it. LOCATION: The Westin Rio Mar is about 40 minutes from San Juan, very close to the entrance of El Junque Rainforest and the Fajardo Biobay (The bioluminencence was stunning-just go on the darkest night possible, by kayak, and use insect repellent!). DO NOT reserve tours thru the hotel as prices are very inflated. You will hear the chorus of the cute Coqui (frogs) at night. Don't forget to explore further south for some great beaches and scenic drives. AMENITIES: Nice bar areas with tropical flowers, tiny casino, terraces, golf, weekend outdoor movies, bakery called Mike's Cookies which is another option for b-fast) Live piano music in the lounge downstairs. In the evenings, candles are lit. We have travelled all over the tropics and would definitely return the Puerto Rico and this hotel in particular in the future. Everyone was friendly and helpful, as were all of the locals we met. Our teenage daughters did not want to leave!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Just a few helpful hints... June 19th - June 24th We have just returned home after a five night stay at the Westin Rio Mar in Rio Grande. The resort is absolutely gorgeous but I do believe that they have a bed bug problem. Each morning my husband and I and our three children (ages 15,18 and 23) woke up with bites all over our bodies. I had read other people's reviews before we went but didn't believe the bed bug concerns. They are true!! If you do stay at the Westin Rio Mar, please take a shuttle from the airport and rent an Avis car from the hotel. It will make the trek to and from the airport sooooo much easier. Do not book tours through the hotel-do it yourself. We went through Eco-tours for a snorkeling outing and saved $35 dollars on each of our tickets. In fact, we followed the Westin's shuttle bus to and from the snorkeling site. With a family of five, we saved a bunch. We also did the Bioluminescent Lagoon tour with BIO BAY Ride, with Captain Miguel Suarez. He has been doing these tours for over thirty years and has great stories and information to share. He makes the experience exceptional. The traffic in San Juan and further to the east is outrageous!!! It takes forever to get to even a location 5 or ten miles away. Please drive defensively because no one uses their signals and people constantly go through red lights. It's really dangerous. There is no need to go to Luquillo beach if you stay at the Westin. The Westin has the most gorgeous beach ever! The Puerto Rican people were very kind and friendly. The service in restaurants and the many roadside stands was extremely slow-even the fast food places took forever. Just be prepared to wait. Old San Juan is really beautiful and a must!!!!

<Author>NYCtraveler-6
<Content>Wonderful!!! Me and my two friends (all women, mid-twenties) went to Puerto Rico in the middle of May. After reading previous reviews, I was very hesitant about staying at the Westin. But it ended up being GREAT!!! We ran into some bad weather, scattered thunderstorms, but we managed to get some sun. As recommended, we did not eat at the hotel (for the most part). We at the pool bar once and that was decent. Generally, we went into San Juan to eat. The Oof Restaurants are excellent! We visited the Parrot Club, Aqua Viva and Dragonfly. They were all wonderful, and I would consider myself a foodie from NYC. Both the service and the food were of high standards and I would highly recommend going there. We also went to the Puerto Rico Cafe, where we had seafood gumbo, which was YUMMY!Like others, I recommend renting a car. It's very easy getting around the island and we never missed a step in our travel plans. Parking was very easy at the hotel and in Old San Juan (park in garages). We visited the El Yunque Rainforest and loved it! If you enjoy hiking and being outdoors, this is the perfect place for you. They have quite a few trails for you to pick and is very easy to walk through. If you do enough research before you go, there is no need to go to the visitors center (you have to pay). We chose to go right to the trails and explored the area ourselves. On one of our days, we went snorkeling on the Spread Eagle II. The group provided snorkeling gear, lunch and complimentary drinks (alcholic and non-alcoholic) for $65. We had such a great time! The staff was very nice and we didn't run into any problems. Our room at the Westin was very comfortable and was kept very clean throughout our stay. The concierge was very helpful in recommending local restaurants and was accomodating when it came to reserving a shuttle back to the airport for one person in our group. The check-in and check-out process was very easy. I'm not sure why the folks who gave bad reviews had such terrible experiences. I couldn't have asked for a better stay at the Westin!

<Author>xqzmi
<Content>Wary at first, but great resort We stayed at the Westin Rio Mar for 5 days. You definitely need to rent a car to get there because transportation by taxi ($60-70) or by shuttle service is too expensive. Getting to the resort was not a problem--go by Rt 66, make a right at Belz Factory Outlet onto Rt 3 and you'll see the sign for the Westin on the left. However, finding the main building in the resort was difficult, especially at night. We saw all the signs telling us, Caution: Iguana Crossing but no clear sign directing us to the hotel. Eventually we hit a deadend and a staff member helped us out. Check-in: Very fast, very smooth, and very patient to answer all our questions. We also had a fridge request (no extra charge) and that was brought to our room in 10 min. Self Parking is very efficient but pricey $10/day. Room: The first thing we did was check for bedbugs after all the reviews we read about that. We were in total paranoia, but we were lucky and there were no bugs in our beds. We were on the first floor...very high ceilings. Standard room, no frills, nice balcony...comfortable. Housekeeping wasn't always reliable. There were days when we didn't get face towels, then the next we didn't get new soap. We literally walked up to the cart and picked it up ourselves because they never delivered it to our room even after we called. Grounds: Very beautifully kept. The maintenance starts early and everything is very organized. There were plenty of towels, pool balls, lounge chairs with umbrellas around the pool. The beach is eh, not the golden sand or clear blue water you imagine of the caribbean but it's still nicely kept. there are cabanas and plenty of lounge chairs there too. They have 2-3 jet skis, kayaks..but all for a price ($60 jet ski for 1/2 hour).they have activities planned everyday that are listed on a bulletin board in the lobby and outside area by the pool (power walk, iguana feeding, dancing). the casino is not very large but it's still fun to just wander around. they have a very large conference room...was not able to see inside, but we did see the outside grounds set up for a wedding. The grass in that area was extremely brown, not exactly pretty. Oh..bugs galore...must wear bug spray everywhere you go. Cannot comment on the restaurants in the hotel except for David's Cookies. We picked up something there for breakfast a couple times before going out. We mostly ate outside of the resort. We went to Las Vegas, which is en route to El Yunque on Rt 191. (El Yunque is literally across the street from Rt 968 and follow the signs to Rt 191). Isamar's bakery on the corner of Rt 968 is very good...their Cuban sandwich is really good. Along the way to Luquillo, we saw all the kiosks numbered but we didn't get to try them. We went to dinner at Sandy's Seafood, really good seafood, large portions of everything. There are plenty of fast food places around especially KFC/Taco Bell and Burger King. We also ate at Antonino's and Taco Maker along Rt 3 (east of resort). If you continue on Rt 3 to Fajardo, you'll hit a shopping plaza with sizzler, metropol, many other restaurants. Concierge: I think this was the best part of the hotel. They have directions to everything, preprinted cards. They were very helpful. However, booking through them, especially tours looks extremely overpriced. Call the tours yourself, it's a better deal. Around the Area: El Yunque is right across the street. Luquillo is a 5 minute Drive and is an overall nice beach. Not sure why it's rated as a great beach but, it is still a nice place to relax..Parking is $3. They have kayaks for rent there and it's only $5 per person...much much cheaper than the resort which was around the range of $45 for 1/2 hour. Check out: bill sent to room with easy check out form. We weren't charged a 13% resort fee--maybe it's a deal they cut out with priceline. I don't know...but i'm not complaining. Overall, this was a very enjoyable resort. It's not a 5 star resort but it was still worth visiting.

<Author>travel2424
<Content>Some issues, but pleasant overall... When I made the reservation online, I booked and specifically paid for (not just requested) a King sized bed. If I went to PR again, I'd stay in Fajardo.Yes, the food was a bit overpriced, but not anymore so than other similar resort hotels. The food was good quality. The best dishes were local. A suggestion--get room service for breakfast in the mornings. The prices are reasonable and you can eat out on the balcony. Although, about half of our room service orders had something not quite right (we were delivered an empty coffee pot one day and the cream was hot another). But the staff was prompt in fixing any errors.One thing I noticed is the place was overrun with kids. The Westin is obviously young kid-friendly, but they must have been running some kind of special for families before the high season began. I don't mind kids, and most of them seemed happy, but had I known how many were going to be there, I probably would've chosen another resort.I probably would not return again, mainly due to the Rio Grande area and lack of things to do around the resort.

<Author>That'sMyOpinion
<Content>Beautiful beach setting, but the rooms and amenities are just ok This hotel is set on a picture perfect beach, and thank God for that, because you will want to be out of your room as much as possible. The beds are comfortable, but the room itself is standard motel. Be prepared to either not use the airconditioning or to freeze your buns off. The airconditiong is set to blow cold air, but not to remove humidity. Therefore, all your clothes will be soggy, and I mean soggy. You will have to launder everything in your suitcase (clean or not) when you return home. The staff tries very hard for the most part, but this is not the Four Seasons, so they do what they can. The casino is a joke and the restaurants are only average. This is our second trip to Puerto Rico to attend conferences. It just is not my favorite island. If spending your own money, shop around a bit more!!
