<Author>Shpilkes
<Content>Exactly as you should expect Spent a week here in April 2006; this was my second trip, as I was there for a week's vacation in the late 1990s as well. I can corroborate the various pros and cons listed in the reviews beneath this one, most of which are accurate and depend on one's perspective and optimism. In sum:- The grounds are beautiful and immaculately kept, particularly for a busy family resort. Rooms are spacious and comfortable, although the Westin Heavenly Bed, while large, was less than heavenly (probably due to the sheets).- Staff are almost universally friendly, although many of them are not as helpful as one would hope, and in random ways. The service can be maddening. Among our random gripes: we had a full plate of bathroom items but no shampoo; turndown service ceased without notice halfway through our trip; and the every 15 minutes shuttle bus often felt MIA. Service express button on the phone is a marvel, but it makes you wonder why the rest of the hotel doesn't run as efficiently. - Restaurants are sub-par but not downright bad. We suspected the restaurant managers are not doing their jobs very well, as the wait staff was not sloppy or embarrassing, just not well coordinated. Do expect to wait pretty much every meal. By the end of the week we had inured ourselves.- Facilities are all very good. Two golf courses with a complimentary driving range, 13 tennis courts, two pools with kid-friendly toys, basketball courts, water sports gear, even a big open lawn for playing ball--despite any frustrations with the way the hotel is run, we never lacked for something to do and always enjoyed ourselves.Was it perfect? Nah. But was it resoundingly good? Yep. I'd go back without complaint.

We have traveled extensively especially in the Caribbean and we settled on this location because of the length of our stay (5 days) and easy flights. I'm pleased to say our stay was great! Was it perfect? No, but very few Caribbean resorts are outside of the Four Seasons at Nevis and Caneel Bay in St. John. This resort is extremely large. We were there over Easter week and it was completely full. Even with that, every service person we encountered had a big smile and tried to be as helpful as possible. Chairs were scarce around the pool areas, but on demand at the beach. My kids had a good time because of all the activities (my sons are 11 and 12). They have a nice gameroom and frequently showed movies at the pool at night with soft drinks and popcorn. My youngest especially loved the nightly bonfire and s'mores!! There is a new highway from the airport (66) so the drive is now under 30 minutes. If you go, try King's Seafood near Fajardo. I recommend this resort highly especially if you have a family!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A wonderful place in the Caribbean!! We just returned from the Westin Rio Mar - were there from Apr 1 - 7. Like most, I was hesitant after reading the reviews, but decided to credit the positive ones - especially of late. We were not disappointed. We did not have a single problem. We did check a cooler as carry on luggage (we filled it with our snorkel gear, etc.) which came in handy - as we shopped at the little corner store and purchased pop, liquor, lunch meat, etc. We had most lunches and breakfasts on our beautiful patio. We only ate at Marabella, a couple of dinners and one breakfast - but our food was great, service was perfect. (Rio Mar Burger and Cuban were excellent!) Our check in was uneventful, and although we were staying on Starpoints - the clerk moved us from a ground floor room, to one higher up so we'd have a better view. it was spectacular. The beach was great, the waves were fabuous for boogie boarding (you can buy one for $15 in the gift shop - the day we left, we gave it to a family who was just arriving and they were thrilled!) We spent two 1/2 days in the rainforest and it was great! If you hike down to the La Mina falls, wear your swimsuit - no place to change down there! No kidding about the Sierra Palm concession - the burgers there are to die for. There is a lot of rain, so when it is clear - head to the rainforest. We boogie boarded and snorkeld in the rain. Only when there was a big downpour did it slow us down! We also rented a car, great for running errands, getting around in the rainforest and finding a place to eat outside the hotel if you choose. (I disagree with all the raves about Rosa's in Fajardo - it was mediocre food, hard to find and expensive - but the rolls were good!) The highlight of our trip was the kayak trip through the mangrove swamp to the biolum bay - Mosquito Bay. You meet the guides and kayak right from the marina at Fajardo, it is an easy kayak trip and you get to jump in when you reach the middle of the bay. It is truly awe-inspiring to be swimming in a pitch black bay and be glowing green the whole time! Really - you don't want to miss this. Take the kids - our four year old loved it! The Westin Kids Club was great, staff there was kind and helpful. This is a typical Caribbean resort, drinks and food are expensive. Save where you can and don't sweat the rest... It is a beautiful place, the staff was wonderful, all the time, every where. We will definately return!

<Rating>3	3	3	-1	2	-1	2	-1	

<Author>Scot in America
<Content>Great Resort We were very, very pleased with the Westin Rio Mar. It is clearly one of the top two resorts in Puerto Rico -- the other being the El Conquistador -- and I would actually rate the Rio Mar more highly based on location (45 minutes from San Juan, rather than an hour and a half for the El Conquistador) and the ease of getting to the beach (at El Conquistador, one must take a ferry out to an island, which is not at all convenient and requires more forethought than I am capable of on a vacation!). I am a frequent business and leisure traveler who often stays at Ritz Carlton and Four Seasons properties, and I would put the Westin just a slight notch below such resorts.Advantages: Notwithstanding some of the reviews below, the service was outstanding; the staff was uniformly friendly and helpful, and everything went extremely smoothly during our stay. The resort is also very well-kept and clean, especially for a Caribbean property; a huge army of workers is constantly picking up any loose wrapper, empty cup, or unused towel. The rooms are very nice, with generally good views in Oceanfront or Oceanside rooms. The beach is excellent -- a broad span of golden sand without other properties in sight, and perfect waves for those who like to body surf or boogie board. Each night there is a bonfire near the beach at which guests can roast marshmallows and, with friendly staff assistance, construct s'mores, which makes it unnecessary to order dessert at dinner! The two golf courses are very beautiful and well-kept, and surprisingly quick to get around on for a resort. My wife and I played twice at Rio Mar, and it took us about three hours each round. Both courses are quite expensive ($165 per round), but these greens fees are comparable to those on all of the island's other resort courses. (Note to golfers: I thought the River Course (designed by Greg Norman) was a much more interesting and challenging course than the Ocean Course (designed by Tom Fazio), and the ocean is not as prominent on the Ocean Course as the name might suggest.)Disadvantages: As others have noted, on-resort dining at the Rio Mar is an expensive proposition, though we thought the food was uniformly very good. Dinner entrees at Palio (the Italian place), Shimas (the Asian place) and the Grille Room were $27-40, and, while dinner entrees were cheaper at Club Coqui (a more casual outdoor area near the ocean), the menu was pretty limited. Marbella (the centrally located casual dining place looking out over the ocean) is actually a good dinner option, as it has a very extensive menu with something for adults and kids alike, and a nice atmosphere in the evening (while the room seems a little stark during the day for breakfast and lunch, the lights are dimmed at night for a very nice oceanfront atmosphere). While on-resort dining is expensive, the prices are comparable to and perhaps somewhat less than the El Conquistador down the road. Also, of course, one need not restrict oneself to the resort itself, as there are off-resort restaurants within 5 minutes of the resort in Rio Grande, Palmer, and Luquillo. I would strongly recommend visiting the cheaper and more authentic Puerto Rican places, such as Sandy's Seafood, King Seafood, and Victor's Seafood, all in Luquillo, or Don Pepe's, just outside the resort on Route 3. A must is to try a Mofongo, a traditional Puerto Rican dish consisting of a bowl made of fried mashed plantains filled with seafood or chicken in Creole sauce, which you can get at any of these places. All of the three aforementioned seafood places also have very inexpensive ($15-20) lobster dishes in which a surprisingly large amount of lobster meat is served in at least 10 different ways, from scampi-style, to Cantonese, to garlic sauce.I would say the principal disadvantage of the Rio Mar is that, like the El Conquistador, it sometimes has groups or conventions, which in my view takes away from the ambience of a place (too many loud alcohol-fueled greetings in the lobby, too many slightly overweight people in tank tops acting like they've never been to a nice hotel before). The groups seem to be more prevalent during the weekend than during the week, so if you are planning only a few day's stay, avoid Saturday and SundayTips: 1. Rent a car. You can do El Yunque for free and have the waterfalls to yourself instead of paying an exorbitant amount to take a bus there. We went at 8 in the morning and had the trails and waterfalls to ourselves for three hours. It also allows you to eat off-resort, which can save a bundle, and to go to San Juan and other cities for nothing. Indeed, the rental car virtually pays for itself vis-a-vis the Westin airport bus, which is $27.50 a person each way. 2. Go to a supermarket and buy breakfast stuff on the way into the resort from San Juan. There is free coffee in the room, and a muffin at the onsite coffee place is $3.50 or so. 3. Similarly, consider running out at lunch to buy Subway or BK for the kids rather than paying the high prices at Marbella or the pool. We figure we saved $300 during the week by doing this, which allowed us to focus our spending on alcohol rather than chicken fingers. 3. Definitely spend an afternoon in Old San Juan and have dinner there (we loved the Parrot Club). 4. Don't book excursions through the resort. We went on a Bioluminescent Bay boat trip to Vieques, and it would have cost $140 per peron, with no saving for kids, had we booked through the resort. By booking directly with Island Adventures in Fajardo by telephone, we spent for precisely the same trip, on the same boat, $50 less per adult and $60 less per kid, for a total savings for a family of four of $220. (By the way, I'd highly recommend this trip.)  
<Date>Apr 3, 2006

All in all we had the best honeymoon and actually thought about staying a few extra days and the staff was nothing but helpful with this request and offered us a great rate BUT we had to come back to reality. If you are planning on visiting the Westin please take this review into consideration. Remember nothing is perfect but the Westin was a great experience and I would visit again in a heartbeat.

The drinks were really good and they'll make whatever you want. Try the Bicardi vanilla with passion fruit juice. We ate at Lolita, which is a Mexican restaurant on route 3 between Luquillo and Farada. The margaritas are the best and food cheap and good. Make sure to try the cheese flan. 4TH DAY - We drove to the rainforest, which is very close to the Westin. My personal feeling is not to take a tour. It's more fun to go drive and that way, you can choose what you want to see. We hiked to the waterfalls and took off our sneakers and got wet. My son went completely in and had a ball. It's so beautiful. For dinner, we drove to Rosa's in Farado(got lost, so make sure you have specific directions) and loved it. The rolls are to die for. I could have eaten a dozen of them. My husband and I had the lobster and my son had the skirt steak. Both were delicious. Don't forget flan for dessert.5TH DAY - Hung out by the beach and had dinner at King's restaurant. This place was recommended by some of the people from the smorkel trip. It was a no nonsense fish place that gets a lot of locals. I had fried snapper, my husband shrimp and my son skirt steak. All was good and reasonable. Had flan for dessert.6TH DAY - Went on a snorkel trip with East Island Excursions. If you book thru the Westin, they charge more. We booked thru the concierge at the villas. Originally, booked for the trip to Culebra Island, but the water was rough that day, so we didn't go there, but closer islands. They refunded $20/person for this. The staff was fantastic and lots of fun. The snorkeling was good and we all had a great time. The buffet lunch consisted of cold cuts, tuna salad, pasta salad, etc. Also, included was free sodas and pina coladas (not frozen) and rum punch. We came back exhausted. For dinner went to Las Vegas, which was recommended by the villas. I was hesitant, due to the name. I thought it would end up being touristy, but that wasn't the case. The food was excellent. For dessert, had a pear soaked in red wine. My husband said it was the best dessert he ever had, and that's coming from someone that works in NYC and gets taken out to really nice restaurants for business. 7TH DAY - Just spent the day at the Westin beach, since it was our last. Relaxed, had a couple of frozen drinks (try the ziggy zaggy) and basically just chilled. For dinner went to Metropol, a cuban restaurant. It was just ok, and the only meal we didn't love. Overall, I loved staying in Rio Grande. Personally, I probably wouldn't stay at the Westin hotel, for people complained about the size of the room and the food. But being in a villa right next door, was perfect. There was always a nice breeze at the beach, that kept it from feeling so hot. The people of Puerto Rico are fantastic and so friendly. The food is good and relatively inexpensive by NY standards. There are always negative comments about the crazy driving here from people returning from a visit. It wasn't bad and no worse than Boston, and definitely better than NYC. Overall, we loved our vist and would definitely go back again. It's the 1st time I ever came back with money, instead of going to an ATM for more.

Jose at Shimas.SIGHTSEEINGTo visit El Yunque, which is the only thing close to the resort, is free, if you rent a car. if you go on the hotel tour, it's $38 per adult with a 10% discount for kids. the rental cars were sold out so we decided to take a cab. We got a 15 pax van and were told it would cost $200! When i went to the concierge she explained that only certain taxis were authorized to enter the rain forest. We got it down to $150 and paid the insane price because we were all packed up and ready to go and the kids were excited. in the end, it was a nice way to go because our driver was a local and took us to places the other tourists didn't go, like a pair of waterfalls that you have to hike a little to get to. the view from the tower is breathtaking.Despite everything I've written above, we had a good time because the kids enjoyed it so much. but if i had my choice, i'd go back to atlantis in a heartbeat. hope that's helpful.

<Content>Expect Nothing, Receive Nothing We booked this hotel as a get away before a cruise. ***WARNING ONE***, the hotel is very very far away from the airport, the cruise docks, and Old Town. But, we finally had a balcony. Upon checkout, the hotel had charged us for breakfast, which was allegedly included in the rate, and shuttle service, which we had already paid for. ***Warning Three*** The buffet breakfast is $19.00 a person! We were then called a liar about breakfast being included in our room rate and asked to produce proof - on the spot. After threatening to raise a stink, the charges were removed. We checked out, took our cruise, and returned home to find all $200 worth of charges were put back on the bill. A month later, after about 5 e-mails and 3 phone calls, they were finally removed from my charge card. ***Warning Four*** Don't pre-pay for anything!!! We feel that the charges were removed at the hotel to shut me up and then re-charged once we left. At no point did the hotel attempt to make up for their booking error nor did they attempt to compensate us for having spent 1.5-2 hours at the front desk trying to fix the situation. The grounds of the hotel were very nice and if you get a good rate on the other rooms, go for it. But I wouldn't pay over $200 a night for this hotel and I certainly wouldn't book any services or inclusions through them directly. You'll get a huge hassle and headache. The food at the hotel was mediocre for the Marbella restaurant and poor for the Asian themed restaurant. These were the only two places we ate. Not what we espected for a Westin nor for a 4-star location. The restaurants are not Vegetarian friendly if you like good food. The staff ranged from incredibly friendly to incredibly cookie-cutter and uncaring. Poorly trained and with no apparant management, any problems are dealt with less than one expects at the price we paid for our room. Our problem with this hotel was not expecting something for nothing, but was expecting getting what we paid for and when we didn't get it, having a chorus of shoulders shrug at our concerns. We tried to be nice  patient about it from the get go - perhaps throwing a fit would have worked better.

It seems to be the norm here, that the service throughout the hotel-- front desk, shops, and restaurant staff-- is consistently poor. Our stay at this property was quite brief as we hiked the rainforest for one entire day, and the next day we were gone from 9-5 for a snorkel trip. It is surprising that even though we spent so little tiime here, we had so many problems. I've never had any problems at other Westins. One positive- they do have a firepit where they roast marshmallows and have smores (free of charge) from 7-10pm. The two staff members here were exceptionally friendly and helpful. (After we checked out and were at the airport preparing to go home.) We called the butler directly at the hotel. He located the wallet and mailed it back to us in the U.S. All money and i.d.'s were intact. The concierge was very nice and arranged a charter for us to spend the day in St. Thomas. We did rent a car and drove to Old San Juan to visit the fort. Once again the staff was helpful with directions. Don't miss a trip to the rain forest, it's worth it! We also drove to another local beach in one of Puerto Rico's neighborhoods. It gave us a real chance to see how the natives live. We stayed at the Westin Key Largo for our honeymoon four years ago and fell in love with it. We would love to go back to the Westin. We loved it and highly recommend you go.

<Content>Not Bad, But Not Great Either I definitely think some of the reviews on this site are a little harsh because while we definitely had some complaints the overall experience was not bad and I had a nice time. Probably easiest to make a list of pluses and minuses:Pluses:- Room was gorgeous, well appointed and clean. Room service was excellent and brought plenty of clean towels, non-allergic pillows and even a light bulb when we noticed one of the lamps was not working. We stayed in a regular garden view room one night and a suite the next two.- Staff was very friendly.- Beach was very nice, especially for swimming.- Pools/hot tubs were gorgeous and clean (definitely not dirty).- The food at the hotel restaurants, while expensive, was very good.- The golf course, although I did not play, was gorgeous. The grounds of this hotel are very well kept and reminded me of South Seas Plantation in Florida.Minuses:- We couldn't get the concierge to either help us in person or return phone calls. A request to make a dinner reservation was forgotten. I don't blame the staff but clearly there are not enough people employed in this capacity to cater to guest needs. - You MUST make reservations every night for dinner or else they'll make you wait until 10 - even if there are available tables. - It is next to impossible to get a drink at the Tiki Bar by the pool, and the waitress service takes forever.- I had a hard time getting drinks at the lobby bars as well.- There isn't much local nightlife. I went with a group of 20-somethings (singles and couples) and there really wasn't much to do aside from the casino. I do think however that it would be a great spot if you have kids.- This is definitely a convention hotel, so there were hoards of people from one company or another milling about the entire time we were there, and the restaurants were clogged with reservations for parties of 30 and 40. Not a lot of attention/sympathy given to individual guests.I probably won't return, but I didn't have nearly as bad an experience as some of the reviewers on this site.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Rio Mar My husband and I and another couple just came back from a 5 night stay at the Westin Rio Mar. It was the best trip we have ever taken to Puerto Rico. We have stayed at the El San Juan, the Intercontinental and the Marriott - all in the San Juan area and there is no comparison to staying at the Rio. We were so apprehensive after reading many of the reviews, but I realize now that many of the people that have written reviews on this hotel are not accustomed to travel in the carribean and to many of the so so accommodations you find there. Having 80 degree weather year round and being on the water takes its toll on many resorts but I must say that this resort does their absolute best to keep the wear and tear to a minimum. The massiveness to the lobby area and relaxation areas around the lobby together with open staircases gives a feeling of carribean luxury. The staff was outstanding. They don't question anything you ask for. Although we could not be upgraded to an oceanview room, we found our rain forest view room to be peaceful and a nice change from the ocean view we normally get when we travel. I found being on my deck in the early morning viewing the mountains and total quietness to be quite wonderful. You must realize that this is a family oriented resort and we were told they only have 20% of their rooms with king size beds. I must say, that the families we saw were quite upscale and with a quiet pool and a family pool it didn't bother us a bit.....and the hotel was full and all restaurants were open.The service was perfect. Our thermostat didn't seem to work properly and by the time I left the front desk and went to my room, an engineer was knocking at my door to assist us. Each night clean towels were put in our room to replace the ones used in the morning. Also, at breakfast I asked for a small amount of milk to use for the coffee in our room rather than the powdered creamer....before I knew it, a water bottle of milk was handed to me, at no charge, which we refrigerated for our coffee. The staff was quick to give us drink coupons for rum drinks if we were inconvenienced at all for the slightest reason.I found only one truthful complaint out of all the reviews I read and that was the cushions on the chairs being damp or wet most of the time. The winter is their rainy season and you can get a downpour for about an hour being so close to the rainforest but then the sun is out shining again. This tends to keep the cushions wet. My second complaint is that the casino leaves something to be desired if you enjoy gambling...Half the machines are inoperable but I don't think this is a big concern because 75% of the people in the casino are locals not guests. I enjoy playing the machines rather than doing the bar thing at night so I would have liked a bit more variety but we visited the other 2 casinos when we rented the car. Plus, I never plan on big time gambling in the carribbean...I save that for Vegas for Atlantic City.The main thing we found impressive is that no one was looking for a handout. At other resorts, there are beach personnel constantly wanting to set up your chairs and get your towels or re-arrange your chairs all for a tip of course. Being a private 500 acre resort there was no one to bother to want to braid your hair or sell you trinkets. No one trying to sell a time share or sell you a boat ride or tour. You get absolute privacy. We chose the transfers with our tour operator for $100 and then rented a car for the middle 2 days at the Avis desk right at the hotel for apprx. $120 for the two days. The ride to and from the airport was about 45 minutes. We had no trouble finding the rain forest, or the other two resorts to check them out...and frankly I am so glad we didn't pick Paridisus or the El conquistador. When we visited these places to go to the casinos, all we saw were jitneys running people all over.All in all it was the most enjoyable trip we have taken and I am ready to book again as soon as I see a good special come around. If anyone has any questions just post your questions and we will be more than happy to respond.... Don't be afraid to go there - it is heaven.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great time! Like many who have written about Rio Mar, I was apprehensive about staying at this resort, almost to the point of eating my plane ticket and canceling my five night stay. This location was recommended by an event planner who works with my wife鈥檚 company, so we went ahead with our travels. The hotel was about an hour drive from the San Juan airport by rental car. We were given an ocean view room on the third floor, which also acts as the main level of the common areas. The room was spacious and clean, comparing well with rooms we鈥檝e recently occupied in the Times Square and Seattle Westins. I usually am not a fan of being stuck in a resort with only the location鈥檚 restaurants to choose from. But, the resort鈥檚 four main dining areas were a nice surprise during our trip, and I looked forward to returning to each. You need to get reservations for these, so plan out your stay with consideration of the days each are open. Though the restaurants may have been half full, I heard the hostess tell guests that they were booked. The first evening we dined at the Grille Room. The crab cakes were so delicious; I ordered a second before my filet arrived. My wife was happy with her meal, although I thought her lobster was a bit overcooked. The second night we ate at Palio, and had a wonderful bottle of Italian wine recommended to us by our waiter. The linguine and clams in garlic olive oil was a great find. Later, we tried Shimas, and though I鈥檓 not a big sushi person, the fare was very nice. We later visited both the Grille and Palio again and were not disappointed. Our only lunch at the resort was at the Pub near one of the golf courses. Like the other sites, the service was great and our waitress had nice recommendations for us. The prices were a few dollars higher than we鈥檙e accustomed to at home, but are typical for any vacation destination.We ventured to the Old San Juan shopping areas during our first full day in Puerto Rico. While getting a rental car is preferred, the pot holes and liberal driving customs do take a bit getting used to. I hit a chunk of loose asphalt on the freeway and won the chance at changing a flat tire on the shoulder of the freeway near the airport. Also, it is wise to count to three when the traffic light turns green before hitting the gas. San Juan is a cruise ship port and as such, is home to many tourist souvenir shops. One which was a bit better was the Puerto Rico Arts and Craft shop, offering the wares of many local artists. On another day we took a visit to the rain forest, which is just across the highway from the Rio Mar. While visiting the Rain Forest鈥檚 Visitors center wasn鈥檛 necessary, it did give us a map which pointed out the area鈥檚 hiking trails. The hike to the waterfalls and pools was very refreshing. We also stopped at the small outdoor restaurant located near the 11 km sign and enjoyed the barbequed hamburgers covered with the owner鈥檚 secret sauce. We took a trip to the El Conquistador hotel located 30 minutes east of Rio Mar. It has a nice hill-side location and we enjoyed taking the funicular down the cliffs to the hotel鈥檚 small harbor and harbor bar. I noticed that several shops on the outer wing of the hotel had a musty smell from water exposure. During the final day of our trip we had planned to hang out by the pool, but a pending storm changed our plans to visit the El Morro fort in San Juan. While we got wet, it was a very interesting trip in which we learned more about Puerto Rico鈥檚 early history. Unfortunately, the storm wiped out our plans to visit the bio-luminescent bay area of Fajardo later that evening.I was very pleased with the staff鈥檚 efforts to make our trip enjoyable. The few shops in the hotel were very nice. I did try out the casino and while a craps table wasn鈥檛 present, I enjoyed my time at the blackjack tables. There are many pleasant areas to have a drink and socialize in the bar and outside most of the restaurants. The pool was better than average, even though my wife had to flee from a native iguana. The beach looks very inviting from the pool bar, but the run-off from the rain forest churns up some of the beach sediments making the waters a bit murky. Overall, we had one of our better trips here, and if you plan on going to Puerto Rico, you should enjoy your time at Rio Mar.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Condos are the best I've been reading the reviews and I agree with the person who recommended staying at the condos. My parents lived in one of the condos for three years and I always loved to visit. This is a very quite part of Puerto Rico. If you want the nightlife, stay in San Juan.If you want the beauty of the rain forest and the quiteness of Rio Grande beaches, I would recommend staying here. I loved the small private pool down by the beach. We would run out to the ocean for a swim and then jump back to the pool. Plus they have a poolside bar. I'd love to get some Pina Colladas.You can find cheap rum there. The local favorite is Don Q (Bacardi is looked on with some distain because they are not originally Puerto Ricans)There are some good local resturants, you just have to look for them. We use to go to this resturant in town called Marebells (I think). My parents went there all the time. My Dad always would get the Arr贸z con dulce. It's a very sweet but tasty rice pudding. The coqui's are all around you and you can listen to their song at night. They are tiny green frogs who chirp coqueee, coqueee and sound like little birds. If you see one, it'll bring you good luck. I saw one right before I left my parents condo for the last time.If you really want to explore Puerto Rico, try to rent a condo for a period of time and drive out to the different areas of the island.

<Content>spectacular This resort is spectacular. Stayed 2 nights in early December 2005. Was immediately struck by the beauty of the location and sheer size of the place. When we checked in we were told that there were no more rooms with king sized beds but they were going to give us a room with two doubles which could be connected to make one super king. A great base for rain forest exploration. The only complaints I have are: the sand flies on the beach (make sure you use lots of bug spray or prepare to be eaten) and the pool could have been warmer. Otherwise, a great experience and I hope to go back there sometime soon.

<Author>jenlara
<Content>Lovely, but a few small critiques I was apprehensive after reading the very mixed reviews of the Westin Rio Mar, but we booked a 3-night getaway here anyway this past weekend, and had a lovely time. First, the positives: the staff were sweet as sugar, and though we didn't have any special needs or requests, I got the sense that we would have been accommodated if we had. Our room, a corner Ocean Suite which was really more just a large guest room, was *beautiful* and exceptionally large, clean, and decorated in a modern, comfortable, understated way. We didn't have much of an ocean view - just a glimpse - but we got over that quickly because the room itself was so nice. The grounds are very well-kept and the two pools are large and clean.The Mandara Spa was really wonderful; I had a massage and a Ginger-Lime Body Scrub, and both were awesome! I've been to many spas, and this one, while not massive like the Golden Door at the Conquistador (it has 12 rooms) was lovely, intimate, and super-relaxing.Now the negatives. The main complaint I personally had was a small one, but important to me: the casino had no craps table. It's the only game I like to play (and I really love it!) so the fact that the Westin goes out of its way to advertise craps on literally every single ad for their casino and on their web site, when they actually don't even have one table, was a huge disappointment.The beach at the Westin isn't the greatest; the sand is brown and coarse, not fine and white. We spend a lot of time in Vieques, PR and are spoiled by the beaches with powdered-sugar sand. The restaurant situation was not great; as many others have stated here, one night there were only two restaurants open for dinner, while another night there were four. The one place that's always open, Marbella, is pleasant enough for breakfast or lunch, but we like to get a little dressy and enjoy a nice dinner out; Marbella just doesn't really cut it. The hotel seemed only about 25-30% full, so maybe that was why they chose not to open all restaurants every night. Still, it was disappointing and we ordered room service 2 of our 3 nights. Palio was just slightly above-average Italian food, and way overpriced, though I do expect that at a resort in the Caribbean.All in all, the Westin Rio Mar is a very nice resort. If you come here with managed expectations, and if playing craps isn't important to you, you should enjoy this beautiful spot.

<Author>kw898
<Content>Don't believe the negative hype As with most message boards you must take the postings with a grain of salt and realize everyone's view is truly subjective. With that being said we just returned from the Westin after a 4 day stay and would recommend this resort. Sure, there are things that are not great, but overall it is a very nice resort.Rooms:We had a ocean view on the 6th floor (Starwood floor). The halls leading to the room were quite musty and outdated (floors also need to be vacummed). The room itself could use some updating, but we were not disappointed. It was spacious, had a nice balcony and was relatively quiet (with the exception with a few door slams). The maid service was great - no complaints.Grounds:The interior of the hotel is very nice. The lobby (which has free wi-fi) was spacious, inviting and was decorated very nicely for the holidays. The pool area was very good and we had no problems getting a seat. They have a quiet pool and a family pool that are both relaiively clean and spacious. Some of the chairs were wet (guess what? - it rains in the Caribbean) so check the lounge before you plant yourself. The beach seemed nice (we spend most of our time at the pool) but the sand is not very pretty (brownish) and the waves are rough.Restaurants:The biggest complaint is here, but keep in mind the hotel was not packed so a few were closed. We went to the Golf Club to eat at the Grille Room and the Iguana Pub (you must take a shuttle there - 5 minute ride - runs very often). The food was ok and the ambiance somewhat limited. The Grille Room was pricey (but what do you expect at a resort?) On Friday night Shimas opened up and we had an oustanding meal and as well as service. The Tiki Bar by the pool was open for lunch (limited menu), but was right on the ocean. Several other restaurants were closed but they should open in the high season when the hotel is booked fully. We did not venture off the gounds to eat, but from what we saw and heard, nothing of great consequence was very close.Fitness Center:Small but has everything that one needs (6 treadmills with TVs, weights, some machines). Towels and water are available.Other Observations and Tips:* Rent a Car! - there is an airport shuttle, but we heard of people who took cabs for $75. Also, to leave the grounds a cab will run you $15 just to get to the gate. The car came in handy for the El Yunque forest. WARNING! - Beware of the local drivers - they are nuts. Signaling does not exist and cars pop out of nowhere. Roads are not easy to figure out. Popping in and out of highway 3 was extremely challenging.* El Yunque was well worth it and 15 minutes from the resort. Wear sneakers as it can be slippery when wet. Do NOT eat at the Visitor's Center. We had nachos and pizza and was one of the top 3 worse meals we ever had. HOWEVER, DO stop by the Sierra Palm Food Concession Picnic Area and get yourself a burger. There's a local that BBQ's up burgers and it was by far the best tasting burger we ever had!!* Casino was very small* Golf course looked great (did not play), but is appeared to be empty everyday.

<Author>barbaradixon
<Content>Some good, some bad The Westin is a top notch hotel, and this hotel is no exception. But it's way overpriced. <Author>saraohara
<Content>Wouldn't go back I was nervous about this resort b/c of unfavorable reviews--but the truth is, it's a nice resort, large, pretty, well-kept. The room was a bit dusty but I suspect that was b/c it hadn't been occupied in a while. The resort was VERY busy and crowded for Thanksgiving week. I wouldn't go back partly for this reason--it's not the kind of place where you are getting away from it all by any stretch of the imagination. The beach is OK, but when we were there the water was muddy as hell b/c the river nearby had dumped debris from recent rains. Food was pretty bad, and way overpriced-and don't kid yourself, it's the same food no matter which hotel restaurant you go to. Pool was nice although $90 for a canopy is a JOKE. Drinks overpriced but strong. One important point to make: I read that the service was terrible--I have to disagree-I received great service the whole time-my only complaint was that b/c we arrived at 4am we were left with the dregs of room choices. All in all, not the nicest Westin property by far, but not a nightmare either.

<Content>Little trip gone bad I've been to Puerto Rico quite a few times and have all ways stayed in San Juan. Don't get me wrong the grounds are very well kept and you can hear the constant song of the native Coqui's. However, nothing is within walking distance. Good thing we rented a car and drove half and hour every day to San Juan for tourist fun.In the End:In the end, I spoke with the day manager and I expressed how unsat this hotel was and that I would never comeback. <Author>shelleyr25
<Content>Rio Mar...nice pool and beach but wouldn't do it again... Stayed at the Rio Mar from 11/22-26 (Thanksgiving week) and found similar problems as had previously been posted in other reviews. To be kind, I will start with the positives. Check-in went smooth on the Tuesday before the holiday but I did see long lines on Wednesday and Thursday. Our room (6126-Oceanview)was kept clean and housekeeping could always be found in the hallway if we needed extra towels etc.. Yes, the beach and pool areas were very nice. Although it was a holiday weekend there seemed to be plenty of lounges available (although the immediate poolside chaises had belongings on them by 8am), I did see staff adding more chaises later in the day so that nobody was without a place to sit. The pool area is very pretty and my kids had a blast on the water slide. There was some construction going on which was a bit annoying (large hoses stretched across the entry area to the beach on Tuesday and Wednesday) they did take a break for the holiday weekend. The beach was nice with plenty of lounges.Because it was a holiday week the hotel was booked solid and with the exception of Tuesday night, all the restaurants were open. There seemed to be plenty of staff whom were all friendly and helpful. All the restaurants have a kids club menu which was great for my picky kids. Now, to my issues...the major one being the food. We ate at Shimas(Asian), Palio(Italian) and the Grill Room/Iguana Pub on the golf course. Shimas was by far the best with the sushi being what I am used to eating at home for about the same price. The biggest let down was Palio...very limited menu with high prices for sub-quality food. I am from the NY area and am accustomed to paying a bit more when I am out to eat but for that I expect to get a good meal. At the Rio Mar I did not. Not for a single meal(other than the sushi) did I feel that it was worth the money that they were charging. We never made it to the buffet breakfast because we do not generally eat a large breakfast and for $18 a person it would not have been worth it. We also did not go to the buffet Thanksgiving meal because at $45/adult and $22/child, I could just not justify spending the money since by Thursday I had already learned enough to know that it just wouldn't be worth it. The restaurants on the golf course did have a bit more of a selection but the calamari looked like frozen onion rings and my $30 roast duck tasted like rubber. The saving grace (stretching it) was the David's Cookie bar in the lobby. It served coffee, pastries, ice cream and snacks. That was where we had breakfast in the morning and ice cream for the kids at night. Once again, the prices were incredibly inflated ($3 for a large coffee!!). The rooms were so-so..although as I stated before, they were kept clean but are in severe need of updating. The bathrooms are out of the 80's and the brown wooden furniture looks like it belongs in a childs room. The public bathrooms in the lobby had already been updated and were in much better shape although it seemed that out of all the stalls only one or two in each bathroom had working locks. Not sure why that problem hasnt been addressed yet because it was truly annoying. A few tips if you will be traveling there: rent a car and use the self-park, bring snacks to eat poolside, dont limit yourself to onsite dining you will be greatly disappointed, bring bug spray and use it all the time, make sure to go to the rainforest in your car without a tour..its free!!Despite the problems, we did have a nice time and met many nice people. The kids had a great time at the pool and beach and really loved the iguana feeding every morning at 11 am. We did have alot of clouds and rain but the kids activity director had many things planned to keep the kids busy. I would not return to the Rio Mar strictly due to my issues with the dining. I enjoy quality food and dont like to feel that I am being ripped off each time I eat a meal. Hope you found this review helpful.Shelley

<Author>everoaks
<Content>Private owned ocean condos at Westin Rio Mar a better deal. First, all lodging in Puerto Rico is expensive and a nightmare getting in and out of San Juan, like Chicago traffic. You can book a rental car for $40 a day. Find a Budget/Hertz/Avis bus outside to bring you to their trailer office. Or if you鈥檙e nervous about driving, the hotel transfers you in their bus for $75 a person. The Westin Rio Mar took over an hour to get to and two hours to get back. They claimed 30 minutes to drive 15 miles. No way. The Westin is one of the nicest resorts in PR. People come here for company conferences and golf outings. It鈥檚 a beautiful, safe, large, and expensive resort. When I couldn鈥檛 get a king bed/standard rate room for their advertised $199 November sale rate, (they wanted over $349 for mountain view which I found is just as beautiful a view), I found that there are privately owned Ocean Villa condos for rent that are part of the resort, 1,2 or 3 bedrooms with kitchen and washer/dryer, but no maid service. You can buy one for $1million or you can rent them through the resort, or cheaper by using theclusters. Get ocean view, not golf view condos. It鈥檚 a broker service for the owners. Bargain with them during slow season. Pedro the concierge gets your keys. Or find an actual owner like we did through vacation rentals by owner. (vbro) We got a 1 bedroom for $300 plus security deposit. The owner Rafael Ocasio spoke broken English, but was honest. The condos are a minute walk west of resort, all facing the beach. Area is more private and quiet than the resort. We can use the complete resort and their pools but they are not allowed to use our private pools. Pools and hot tubs are clean, but maintenance hoses the chairs every morning, so the cushions are always soggy. Beach is fun to walk. You can find sand dollars if you don鈥檛 break them picking them up. Save money and get your groceries/liquor cheaper at the white corner building at stoplight. Building looks seedy but is safe. My last note of caution is the sand flea. They鈥檙e at every beach in PR. Locals call them Mimi鈥檚. You never see them or feel them bite. Later your legs are infected with itchy blisters. Always wear bug spray, even by the pool or be sorry.

<Content>A great hotel! Ignore the negative reviews, some will complain about anything! We are returning for our 3rd straight year this March. My husband and I and our now 8 yr old daughter have stayed at the Westin Rio Mar for the last 2 years in February/March. We stay at the Westin for 6 nights and then go down to the Ritz Carlton in San Juan for the last 3 nights. (The Ritz is also spectacular!!!) We've met some great families here and our daughter loves it every time. You are not going to find a better beach or location!!! This is definitely a great family place to be. People in other reviews have complained about the lack of night life but his has not been an issue with us. We still manage to be walking around and having with our daughter and having fun at 10 pm!! We've driven over and visited the Wyndam El Conquistador just to look at it. Yes it is certainly grand and massive but I certainly did not feel like I was missing out on anything at the Westin....especially having to take a ferry everytime you wanted to go to the beach!! The beach and water at the Westin is beautiful and you will be hard pressed to find a better one any where this side of the island. People who complain that the sand isn't white better get over it cause there are no white sand beaches this side of the island starting as far down as San Juan!! It still feels like velvet and they comb it every morning. The water and waves are great for swimming. Once it was pretty rough due to the winds but even then it was still fine for swimming.FOOD- Why does everyone act so surprised at the cost of food and drinks? Of course theyre going to be more than what you're use to paying in your local hometown! But you did to chose to vacation at a nice hotel and the nicer the hotel the more you'll pay. The prices are no higher at the Westin than they are at any other 4 star hotel. Your on vacation, just forget all the nickel and diming and enjoy yourself!!!! There will be plenty of fine food to be found here. You can also go to the local resteraunts which are great too! The bartenders in the lobby bar have great recommendations for where to go.ROOMS - Our rooms have been wonderful, and believe me, I'm a snob when it comes to hotel rooms!! Only on our first visit did we experience a problem with our room and it was due to the noise. We had a mountain view ( which is beautiful too) but our room was directly over the front entrance so we had to listen to the hotel shuttle and all the cars and people coming and going all the time. We talked to the Manager and they moved us the next day without any problems to a different room and it was great. Housekeeping was always great and friendly and the rooms and bathrooms were great with hairdryers etc. And the Heavenly Beds, well they are really heavenly!! RENT A CAR!!!!! Rent one at the airport upon arriving and keep it for the trip. You will save an exorbitant amount of money doing it this way. Getting one at the hotel which run around $60 for a day and you still need to pay for transportation to and from the airport. We rented from Thrifty for a week and it was only $180!!!! Getting to the hotel and getting around is actually very easy. The worst thing is the traffic sometimes. There is a $5 daily parking fee at the hotel, but well worth it....come and go as you please. There are gas stations really close to the hotel. Great resteraunts just a short drive away from the hotel and on the way up to the Rain Forest which is literally across the street!! It is impossible to please everyone but I will tell you this is a wonderful hotel!!!! Yes, I'm sure you can always find SOMETHING or SOMEONE that you didn't like, but that would happen no matter where you stayed. We look very forward to coming back in March!!!!!!!!!

It also didn't have that same  Nickle and Dime- take advantage feeling that I got at the El Conquistador. The staff also seemed much more attentive. If you go, defintely rent a car, its easy to get to and gives you so many more options in case of bad weather. I would go back, I just hope for a little better weather.

I looked at the reviews after I had booked the Westin and frankly, I was a little scared. However, I don't think the prior reviews did it justice. We arranged with the hotel to have the shuttle pick us up at the airport. The greeter was waiting for us and was extremely friendly. The shuttle driver acted as our tour guide to the hotel, again extremely friendly. As a matter of fact, everyone from the front desk staff to the waiters and baggage porters could not have been friendlier. The hotel grounds were immaculate. The pool was great although the water could have been kept a little cleaner. We rented the cabana for 1/2 day ($30), well worth it. They give you a cooler of drinks, chips, pretzels and fruit. The rooms were the typical hotel room, however, the beds and pillows are worth the stay. The restaurants again are the typical Caribbean restaurants - high priced and ok food. If you don't expect home cooking and home prices, you will be ok.The down side: Once there, unless you rent a car or pay enormous amounts for the tours (Old San Juan - $50 pp; Rain Forest - $40 pp and the Bio Bay Tour - $130 pp), you are stuck there. There is one store for a little shopping for some souveniers. There are no buses to take you anywhere and if you want to go into San Juan by taxi it will cost $160.00 round trip for up to 4 people. You have a choice for breakfast of either the buffet, room service or a donut at Davids; the outdoor pool restaurant or Marbella for lunch and 5 restaurants for dinner - two off site that you get to by shuttle. If you need to take the shuttle to the hotel from the airport the price is a standard $145.00 round trip for 3 people.If you are looking for a quite place to do nothing but hang out, swim and take long walks on the beach, this is your place. If you have kids who might be looking for a little more action and might get a little stir crazy doing nothing but relaxing, then the Westin will not meet your needs. All and all - the Westin was a very nice experience.  
<Date>Sep 2, 2005

<Author>snoopy76
<Content>Enjoyable Trip We stayed at the Westin July 18 - July 22, 2005 and we had a wonderful time. This was our 3rd trip to Puerto Rico; we previously stayed at the Wyndham El San Juan. The Westin is a lot quieter than the El San Juan but we had an enjoyable time. The hotel was very clean and well kept and the grounds were manicured beautifully. The beach was beautiful and clean but the sand isn鈥檛 white. We had a Mountain View room, which had a beautiful view of the Rain Forest.We opted for the all-inclusive package, I鈥檓 glad we did because the food and drinks are pricey. The all-inclusive package includes all food (hamburgers, to prime rib and lobster) and premium liquor. I would suggest making dinner reservations as soon as you arrive. Room service is also included with your package without an addition fee. Make sure you receive a brochure of how to fill out your receipt for your food/drinks when you check in, so you will not be charged addition fees.Marbella was good for breakfast; breakfast consists of a buffet and omelets cooked to your taste. Marbella was good for lunch, you can choose from the buffet or from the a la carte menu (burgers, sandwiches, salads, ect). You can also enjoy lunch poolside at Club Coqui. Our favorite restaurants for dinner were The Grill Room at the country club, the prime rib, lobster, and shrimp were delicious. Palio had good Italian food and an excellent Caesar salad, which is made at your table. Nightly entertainment consist of a Casino and a good one man band in the lobby area, where people can dance. Downstairs outside Palio is a piano bar which is nice and relaxing.I would suggest renting a car for about $60 a day or a driver/taxi for tours. The Old San Juan tour is $48 per person from 9-3. It was 4 of us so we got a driver/taxi and it was $160 to Old San Juan. We also had the same driver to take us around Rio Grand. Our drive name was Louie, be sure and ask for him, tell him the Texas gang said hello.

<Author>cindycinn
<Content>A Few Helpful Hints The resort itself is gorgeous!! It looks just like the pictures.Just a few helpful hints.....1. There IS a shuttle from the aiport to the hotel (and back). It's $27.50pp one-way. Make arrangements thru the hotel prior to arrival. When we called the hotel inquiring about transportation we were told there was NO shuttle and that most guests take a taxi for $80 ONE WAY. Mis-communication or lie? I'm not sure..... The ride takes anywhere from 30 minutes to an hour depending on traffic.2. If you need a microwave or refrigerator you MUST request one be placed in your room, provided one is even available. The mini-bar fridge isn't cold; so don't think you'll be able to empty it and put your things in and then put the mini bar stock back later. We had a fridge delivered to our room. We placed our left-overs (from a delicious off-site restaurant called Metropol) in the fridge and went to bed. The next afternoon, after a visit to the rainforest, we returned in hopes of some really delicious left-overs. What we found was a fridge that didn't work, ruined food, and a horrific smell. (rotten fish!) Management did compensate us the food cost but we'd already returned our rental car and could not return to Metropol for more.... Heartbreaking, to say the least.Also, they CHARGE $35 per stay to have a microwave placed in your room. I'm not certain how much for the fridge, though.Lastly, on our first night there I called and asked if there was a microwave anywhere on site that I could use. I was told NO. I asked again So, there's not even ONE microwave anywhere on this entire property? Again, she said NO. Mis-communication or lie? Again, I'm not sure....3. The Quiet Pool doesn't exist. There are two pools within very close proximity and the kids are EVERYWHERE!! MARCO!!!!!!! POLO!!!!!!! It's quieter on the beach.4. If you're planning on spending the extra money for a Governor's Suite, please don't. It's not any bigger or better than a regular room. One of the hotel employees gave us a tour and I wasn't impressed.....5. The Casino and bar area tends to be quite smoky. If you're allergic or sensitive to smoke (as I am) you'll enjoy the east wing first floor piano area a little bit better. Though you won't be near the action. 6. Oh and before you spend $3.00 on a bottle of water in the gift shop. There's FREE bottled water in the fitness center. Help yourself!!! :o)Just a few helpful hints...... Enjoy!!

<Author>harrington
<Content>Upscale, luxurious, Italian marble  A perfect trip for our family. My children are ages 6  8 years old. Combined education in the rainforest, which is a U.S. National Park by the way, relaxation in comfort, and shopping  dining in Old Town. Plus this was a perfect time of year to visit! Don't be scared off if rain is forcast. We were dissappointed to see the forcast on weather. It was rain for our entire stay. What we found was that there was typically, a very brief and refreshing shower (less than 1/2 hour) on some days. Although the hotel was bustling, we could always find an umbrella on the beach and shade at the pool. The beach is expansive and deep. The pool photos on the hotel website is exactly what you get. We have stayed in 4  5 star hotels in Thailand, Greece, Paris, Hawaii... The beach cannot be compared to Hanalei Bay on Kauai, but, that's the best there is. As you enter the hotel grounds, you know you have arrived in an oasis of manicured gardens, flowering shrubs, the whole bit. The restaurants were overpriced for mediocre food. We had expected local fruit, but, it seemed to be more standard Westin cuisine to me. But, we did eat most meals there for convenience, unless we happened to be in Old Town. We rented a full size car from National for a week and were lucky enough to get one with only 5 miles on it. Perfect for driving from the Westin to Rincon for a two night stay in a Parador. The highways were much like the ones here. The Parador (Casa Islena) was highly rated on travel sites, but, we found it a relief to be back in that Heavenly Bed at the Westin! Service was about average and fine. As in any foreign country, I've found that if you treat the staff without arrogance, you will pleasantly surprise them!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Overall, a good vacation. Just returned from a 5-night stay with my husband and 7-year-old son. We did have a very nice vacation, but the irritations we had were hotelrelated. The Up Side: Beautiful location, gorgeous water and beach, friendly (albeit mostly ill-informed) staff, nice pools, wonderful beds, nice large room. The rain forest and snorkeling excursions we took were great! It is a quiet place...not much in the way of hopping nightlife, but we don't care about that, so it worked for us. The Downside: Our buffet breakfasts (which were quite nice) were included with our package, HOWEVER, all of the other food and drinks were grossly overpriced and unexceptional in terms of preparation/taste. $50 for a no-alcohol-or-desserts poolside sandwich lunch for two adults and a hotdog-eating kid? $10 for three cookies from the snack shop? $8.50 for an 8-oz margarita in a plastic cup? Our solution was to take a $30 ride to the nearest grocery store and buy a couple of six-packs of Fosters, bottled water, sodas and some snacks. Given the money we saved on just the beer ($14 for 12 bottles versus $82--tip included-- had we bought them at the hotel, we came out way ahead, even after the $30, 10-minutes-each-way cab ride)One evening, we went to Cactus Jack's (Tex Mex) for dinner and could only be seated at the bar, which was okay by us since we hadn't made reservations. During our meal, there was the intermittent smell of sewer gas which the waitresses told us came from the tennis club bathrooms situated below the bar. To combat the stench, they were spraying air freshener in the bar area while people were eating! When we returned to the main hotel, I spoke with the manager in charge who simply said Sorry. Given the cost to stay at the Westin, I expected more in terms of responsiveness from the management (maybe a free drink?) The grounds are lovely, but the hotel seems to have maintenance issues..for example, we were on a Starwood Preferred Floor and noticed many big spots of paint missing from hotel room doors, even on the Ocean Suite doors. In our bathroom, the showerhead dripped heartily when we ran the tub for a bath, tub faucets and temp control hardware appeared to be unsecured/ uncaulked...they moved around on the wall when we turned the handles. And the curved shower curtain rod sagged downward. Also, the hotel was full when we visited and this caused problems in trying to find on-site places to eat at reasonable times (i.e., not 10 pm). Understandable. We went to Marbella at 6pm and were told no tables 'til 10pm, we then went to the pool restaurant and were told by the manager how about 9:45, or you could try Ajili Mojili..you won't need a reservation. We then went to the concierge who called ahead to Ajili Mojili for us and found out that they were, in fact, closed on Friday night. Then the concierge recommended Antojitos Puertoriquennos (a restaurant off the property, where we had eaten previously). We went to the head doorman (Juan...who was great) and he told us Antojitos had closed at 5pm, but he sent us to another restaurant (Richie's) which was great AND they sent a car to pick us up (no charge) because they knew that the Westin had no car-service vehicles available. Also, we did not rent a car and ended up feeling like Westin prisoners. Whenever I asked for a taxi at the front door, I was given a car-service type vehicle (i.e., had an arrangement with the hotel) and every trip cost $15 each way...even a 10-minute drive! It was nuts! Given that bus service outside of San Juan seems to be nearly non-existent and there were no sidewalks, we felt stuck. If we were to return, we would definitely rent a car and suck-up the $15/day parking fee (on a 480-acre property, please, it's not like they have limited space).Finally, the early-morning-chaise-lounge-reserving by people who never showed up was extremely annoying...the hotel should do something about this. It is obnoxious and unfair to the other guests. Other resorts I have stayed in have had no problem in posting signs and removing people's towels from lounges that go unused.WOULD WE GO BACK TO THE WESTIN??? Maybe, but we would definitely rent a car and consider renting a condo on the property so we would still have access to the casino/beach/pool/spa/restaurant amenities but more control over what/where/when we ate. I really do not mind spending money to eat while on vacation, but I would prefer to spend money to help the local economy rather than the Westin economy! Everything seemed very calculated to generate the maximum amount of money for the Westin as possible...as an example, no happy hour or drink specials at the beach bar and $2 for a tiny bag of popcorn next to the hotel playground, tiny ice buckets that made it hard to chill anything that did not come from the mini bar. It is a beautiful location...there is no denying that. And we came back relaxed, which was the objective.

<Content>Underwhelming Usually love Westins (had a great experience at their St. John one a few years back), and was very much looking forward to this visit (January 05). <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great place, needs improvement We stayed at the Westin Rio Mar in early March 2005. The resort is gorgeous, the grounds are spectacular. The service upon our arrival was outstanding. The bellhopes made it a point to make us feel welcome.The room was nice, but it was a disappointment to have been told we'd have an ocean view room and to see only a teensy bit of the sea due to the enormous palm trees blocking our view. Otherwise, the room was very nice, big enough, and the bathroom was clean and in great condition. The HEAVENLY BED at the Westin are exactly that: heavenly. Best nights' sleep I'd had in a long time. It was great to open the sliding glass door and be lulled to sleep by the sound of the ocean waves.The refrigerator that was part of the minibar didn't work, so anything in there was lukewarm, forcing you to have to go downstairs to get something or have it sent up via room service.The maid staff who serviced our room was spectacular. We were there with a group, and it had been arranged that the maid staff would go to the rooms during the day to drop off favors for conference attendees. If they came in after having serviced the room and we'd messed up the beds, they fixed them a second time. In the evenings, when they knew we would most likely be at a planned activity, they'd come in and bring a bucket of ice for us.I disagree with the reviewer who said there's nothing nearby. Just a short drive away are pharmacies, fast food joints (Burger King, McDonald's), and an outlet mall for the shoppers out there.I do, however, agree with the reviewer who commented on the food at the restaurants on the resort. Palio in particular was an enormous disappointment. I so seldom turn away food that it was shocking to me that I couldn't eat the $14 gourmet pizza I ordered. The three other people in my group that evening were totally unimpressed with their meal choice as well. Even though I didn't complain or send back my meal, when the waitress came by to ask if I wanted the pizza boxed (I ate half of one slice) and I said no, thank you, no follow-up was made to take it off the bill.The rest of the food we ate was for the attendees of our group, and even though it was boring (same breakfast every day, very similar lunches every day), it was adequate when it came to food. It was annoying, however, when the wait staff would hardly wait until you'd cleared your plate to descend on your table to take it away. On more than one occasion I had to tell them that No, I'm not finished yet.My biggest complaint is that their Kids Club is AWFUL. The two people who were there on the one night I used their services were obviously bored to tears and did absolutely nothing to attempt to engage my son in conversation (not even Hi! What's your name?), let alone play. When we arrived they were watching soap operas on the tv and when I returned to pick up my son, he reported that he'd asked them to play with him and they'd said they were busy. The sat him in front of the tube and played the movie Shrek (which nobody asked ME if that would be okay) during my absence.Would I stay there again? Yes, provided there was an improvement to their Kids Club and to their food quality and selection.

<Rating>4	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>wise2374
<Content>Overall - impressed. A lovely upscale resort. My wife and I returned from a quick three night jaunt to the Westin. We came away impressed, and if we're to return to Puerto Rico, it's likely we'd stay here again.THE GOOD: The property and hotel are lovely. The public spaces are all tastefully done and attractive - a large lobby area has a number of cool seating areas and a bar and overlooks some of the restaurants on the level below. The casino is relatively small but very lively.We were happy with the rooms, which are standard Westin, and therefore a touch nicer than the average Caribbean room in resorts of similar caliber - they're nice sized, have an outdoor balcony with a table and chairs, and have all the fixings you'd expect from a Westin - including a couch, handsome desk and the heavenly bed. The bathrooms are really very nice, with a great shower and separate room for the toilet.The outoor areas are nicely done as well, with landscaping that's very pretty but not overdone. There are essentially two large pool sections - one right next to an outdoor bar/lunch restaurant and the (annoying) music that comes with it, and another further away that's much quieter. The pools are very nice, with plentiful chairs bordering it. The exterior of the hotel was attractive as well - it looks like the upscale resort you're paying for.By far, the reason to come here is the beach, which, compared to the beaches we've been to in San Juan, is the nicest we've seen in Puerto Rico. As it's 45 minutes from San Juan, the hotel is in a relatively secluded area and its beach stretches for a mile or so - and it's beautiful. Puerto Rican beaches aren't white sand, but the water is beautiful, there are plenty of chairs, and it's deep enough that you can easily find a spot without people right on top of you. Great, great beach (complete with wait service, should you want it).Finally, there are a number of bars to choose from located in different parts of the resort - plenty of different places to sit an enjoy a drink or cigar.THE BAD: The hotel is something of a trek from the airport: 35 min - 1 hour, depending on traffic - which could be longer if you're taking one of the shuttles included in your package. We chose instead to take a taxi for the speed of it, and that costs roughly $65 each way with tip. (If you do this, make sure you ask your travel professional to take out the airport transfers from your package - which cost extra $$.) The road there looks more like you're on the outskirts of Miami than somewhere Caribbean.The service is hit or miss. It ranged from very friendly and accommodating to I'm annoyed that you're asking this of me. Overall, more good service than bad, though.Finally, once you're there, it's likely you're staying there. Other than being adjacent to El Yunque (the rainforest), there isn't anything worth seeing or doing in the immediate area. Other restaurants are a cab ride away minimum, and there aren't many options.THE UGLY: As you've no doubt read by now, the restaurants do leave something to be desired. Don't get me wrong - none of the food is inedible or scary, and some of it is pretty good stuff. But more often than not, it's completely generic and expectedly very pricey. Worst of all, none of the seafood at the resort is locally caught - all of it is flown in, we learned, and therefore more expensive and not as fresh as you'd like.There are a number of restaurants to choose from - which is nice - and they're located all around the sprawling resort (some of which you'll access by a trolley). But the biggest disappointment was Palio - their destination Italian restaurant. The room itself is really fun and attractive, but it pretty much ends there. The tomatoes in my wife's $16 pomodoro were incredibly mealy - to the point where we actually sent it back. We ordered room service one night (from their full service Marbella restaurant) and the hamburger was of surprisingly poor quality. The lunch menu is pretty spartan, with no good salads and sandwiches that were so-so at best.We did enjoy Ajili Mojili - a Puerto Rican restaurant that is an outpost of the original in San Juan. We've eaten at the original, which is better than this watered down version, but it was still the best and most interesting meal we had while there.There is also a Tex-Mex and an Asian restaurant there, but we didn't try either. The $20 lo mein wasn't calling us.A hint: either load up on their adequate buffet breakfast ($18) in the Marbella restaurant and skip the marginal lunch options, or hit the David's Cookies adjacent to the casino, which has hot breakfast sandwiches, yogurts, muffins, coffee, etc. for a lot less.If we'd stayed longer than three nights, the restaurants would have been more of a problem.OVERALL: Due to the lack of interesting food at the resort and the inaccessibility of other places, a seven night stay can get a little long. But the good in this resort outweighs the bad, in our opinion, and if you're looking for a very nice resort with a great beach in Puerto Rico, you'll be hard pressed to find a nicer spot than the Westin.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good But Would Find a New Hotel Next Time My husband and I recently returned from a week at the Westin Rio Mar. I will start with the positives:-The staff was very friendly, (even if they had no idea what they were talking about)- The beach and pool area were very nice, and you can take long walks on the beach if you are willing to leave the hotel area-The golf course was well maintained and the clubhouse is quite nice- The ice cream at David's was really goodIt goes without saying that resorts overcharge for food, drinks and services so I'm not basing my negative comments on pricing. The bathrooms were certainly not on the same heavenly level as the Westin in Boston or Chicago.-My husband mistakenly left several poker chips in the room one morning. When we returned a few hours later they were gone. We did not make a big deal out of this but reported it to security for their records. They launched into an initial CSI investigation mode, but we never heard from them again. Use the safe.-The Concierge desk was friendly but full of misinformation. They do not have a clue about where to dine outside of the resort. Their literature claims that the rainforest is 10-19 miles away. It is 2 miles away. They told us that a cab to the airport would cost $70 + $15 per person. It cost $60. Again, not a big deal, but doing your own research is worth the time.- The hotel had 2 conventions going on at all times, which adds an institutional feel to your experience. When we arrived the first night, the bar overlooking the ocean was closed for a private party, and the afternoon we left, the pool area closed at 2 PM for another private party.For a big, convention type hotel, the experience was perfectly fine. If we choose to return to Puerto Rico, we would stay in a smaller hotel with a nice beach, closer to San Juan. Does anyone know of one? OR, go to Culebra.

On the positive side, the resort is gorgeous, but in the middle of nowhere. The beach is okay - I'm not used to dirt beaches. It was an okay place for a couple of days before our cruise, but we would never return to this resort or Puerto Rico.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Consistently inconsistent We just returned from a week at the Rio Mar and here is the skinny on our experience. At this hotel the whole is less than the sum of its parts. But it is not a bad place to spend a week.The rooms: Standard, smallish, nothing special - and if you want a fridge it will cost you $65 a week (mini bar in the room though). The staff: By and large we found the STAFF to be warm, helpful, and welcoming - particular kudos to Shelly Ann and Erich who are part of the pool staff/kids activities groups. Wait staff, particularly at breakfast was warm and welcoming.Security: I had $200 taken from my wallet in my room on our first night there - the safe was not working and we had not had time to get it fixed so there was no secure place to stash our valuables. I reported it to security and management, and response was very slow. After 3 days we found out that they refunded me the $200 to my room account, but the only reason we figured it out was because we were scrolling through our room account on the TV menu - otherwise they would have never informed us of this. New computerized safes were installed a few days before we left so that may address this problem. Management: See my comment under security!Food: Ok but not great and very expensive. Our best meal was had at Cactus Jacks which is on the property. If you can get a deal with the breakfast buffet included - do it. We would gorge at breakfast and then only need to purchase dinner.Spa: Really quite beautiful and brand new. The therapists and aestheticians were excellent. however, the reception staff is woefully uninformed about the services, and could never answer my questions about services. Also - some of the services listed in the brochure are not available.Pool: Excellent and big - really nice water slide too. Lots of fun watching iguanas around the pool area, and the kiddie pool is great for kids -(between 130 and 230 they have organized games there). There is also a quiet adult pool - nice for those who don't want kids. The spa tub was not working properly on some days - but when it was - it was nice and large! Ocean is a few steps away , but a little choppy for small children.Casino: Small - less than desirable blackjack rules (can only double 8,9,10,11), dealer does not check for blackjack first so you may play out a hand and waste doubles and splits.Other fun stuff here - iguana feeding at 11, rainforest a few minutes away, bioluminescent bay near by (consider booking excursions on your own - very expensive when done through hotel), consider Old San Juan day trip - try and do it on a weekend as traffic stinks on weekdays.Have fun!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Beautiful, full-service resort Having stayed six nights over the Thanksgiving weekend, with the hotel occupancy 98% on some nights, we liked the view from our upgraded top floor (7th) corner room. All rooms have balconies, those on the 7th floor are recently redecorated. Rooms on South/West side face extensive resort grounds, with the rainforest mountains in the background. Only from the top floor, however, the ocean view is unobstructed. Mostly, the view is partial ocean and swimming pools. Although that is pleasant, it does not stand up to the oceanfront description. One can hardly see any ocean through the palm trees from lower floors. We were first upgraded to a 5th floor Ocean Suite that was not impressive - fairly dark, and not much of the view from the balcony. The hotel is big - over 700 rooms, but we had no problem finding empty beach chairs, enjoying the sea. Staff are really friendly, helpful, willing to listen and help. Room service was offered twice daily, parking rate was 10$, and 50$ return airport shuttle was available too. Food was expensive for Puerto Rico, but not for an isolated, major hotel chain resort. For better value, try a popular Mexican restaurant Lolita - 5 miles towards Fajardo right on Highway 3. The resort seemed ideal for families with children. There were always lifeguards at the beach and pools. For the romantic experience a private dinner is offered on the beach; we saw a table one night with candles among the palm trees on our way to the garage.... For a honemoon, that seems like a good option. San Juan should not be missed, however, and the hotel is not convenient for the city. It is at least 45 minutes drive on a road that gets jammed occasionally. Hotel also offers day trips at somewhat inflated prices. Free breakfast for Platinum Starwood guests with drinks and appetizers in the evening is a nice perk. The gym is free for all and is modern, has elipticals, treadmills, free weights, and around 8 weight machines. Hotel grounds are ideal for jogging and perhaps a bike ride. Overall, a great place.
