<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great experience at the Rio Mar My daughter and I just returned from a long weekend at the Rio Mar and we had a great time. We are not seasoned travelers and were apprehensive as to the logistics of the trip but we were immediately put at ease. When we arrived at the airport, we were greeted by a representative from the hotel's transportation service who directed us to the shuttle van. In fact the Rio Mar is the only hotel on the island with its own transporation service. The driver was friendly, informative and avoided the traffic jam on the highway. Our check in was quick and our room was located on the main floor (3rd) which was very convenient to the restaurants, pools and spa. The guest room was very clean and the beds were heavenly. Every room has a balcony which was wonderful as in the evening it was nice to sit and listen to the sea and feel the warm tropical breeze. We found that the pool and beaches were not crowded and very clean. The restaurants were enjoyable. From Club Coqui to Aliji Mojili, the food and service was excellent. We especially enjoyed the breakfast buffet with the wide variety of food including omelets and the daily specials. The food was priced on the high end but it was expected. The resorts has tours available to the rainforest and many other activities which are arranged at the conceirge's desk. We took the catamaran/snorking and we had a wonderful trip. All in all we had a memorable stay at the Rio Mar and would not hestitate to stay there again.

I very nearly called to cancel the trip and stay somewhere else. I am so incredibly happy that I didn't.Upon arrival at the airport, we were greeted by a Westin representative and once our bags were procured, we were taken to their air-conditioned bus and offered bottles of cold water. After waiting for a few minutes for some more guests to arrive, we made the 40-minute trip to the hotel. The place was gorgeous. First, I'll start with the hotel itself. The furnishings, and the general ambiance was great. Everything had a very tropical, elegant feeling to it. We waited for about five minutes on line to check in, and it went very smoothly. We, along with our bags (all of the luggage, except for the golf clubs which were immediately taken to the clubhouse), rode up in the elevator with a bellman who was incredibly nice and informative. Our room was great. It wasn't huge, wasn't incredibly luxurious -- but it was clean and comfortable (not to mention the infamous Heavenly Beds -- definitely worthy of their name). Our view was amazing. A straight view of the grounds and the ocean beyond. The balcony was adequate and had two comfortable chairs and a matching table. One of my traveling companions (the golfer) was interested in getting in a round before dinner, so he called the clubhouse. This is where we ran into a snag. They were having a tournament that day, and he was unable to get on the course -- either course. Here's a tip: If you are a golfer, when making your reservations, call the hotel to find out if there are any events at either of the courses during your stay (there are two -- the river course, and the ocean course). Since neither of the golf courses are owned by the hotel (they have a share in them that allows golfers from the Westin access), you have to make sure that there are no events scheduled. He went downstairs to speak with the manager. She was polite and apologized for the inconvenience, giving us two free lunches the next day. Should she have given him a free round of golf? Yeah, she should have. But she didn't. Hence the four-star rating rather than a five.Once getting over that hurdle, we went downstairs to a restaurant called Marbella. Marbella is the casual dining, everyday place. It's pricey, yes. But you have to expect that when going away. If you go to a resort thinking that you can be frugal, your naivete is going to get you into trouble. These places are expensive. The food was great, the service impeccable. If you do decide to go, ask to sit in Juan's area -- he's there for breakfast and lunch. The grounds were amazing. Meticulously cared for, and absolutely stunning. We're normally beach people, but we weren't big fans of the sand quality (it's a little muddy), so we spent most of our time under a cabana tent by the quiet pool. Here's another tip: Get down there early if you want one of the two available cabana tents. We're early risers, so it was great. There are umbrellas that you can sit under, but the tent was pretty awesome.A previous reviewer mentioned that the iguanas were like dogs, and they were right. It was pretty amazing to see these dinosaur like creatures waddle out from the surrounding greens and walk along the pool area. We even saw a few of them take a dip in the pool! They don't bother you -- much preferring to nibble at some of the grass than take a bite out of a tourist. They're so used to having people around that it almost seems that they stop to pose for pictures, of which many were taken.At the pool area, waiters and waitresses frequently stop by to ask if you want a drink, or some food from the Coqui bar (named for the famed Coqui frogs). They even carry laminated menus with them for those not familiar with the food selection. If you go during the summer, you have to realize that it is the off-season. This is when hotels do repairs. It's the price you pay for lowered rates and a less crowded atmosphere. We were a bit disappointed that the italian place, Palio, was closed. But we did go to the Asian restaurant, Shimas, and had some amazing food. We're generally casual diners, so we spent most of our nights at Marbella. They have buffets on several evenings, and did have a selection from Palio available. We got some amazing Italian food. If you go when it's open, I highly recommend it.Before I finish my rambling, I would like to say that we had a great time. We are definitely going back next year, and I highly recommend this resort. If you find that the service isn't to your liking, try to smile. Be extra friendly. I work in the customer service industry, and I'll tell ya -- a smile goes a really long way towards improved service.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Don't expect too much My boyfriend and I just got back from Puerto Rico (our first time visiting) and we stayed at the Westin Rio Mar for 4 nights. It's an ideal location if you intend to tour the northeast part of Puerto Rico (El Yunque, Luquillo beaches, Las Croabas biolumenescent bay). The hotel services were good, staff were courteous and facilities were clean. During our stay, we found that the pools were cleaned on a daily basis, which was a plus due to the heavy usage. Since there were two pools, we were able to get away from the kids by utilizing the smaller pool (without the slides). Like someone else mentioned, you should go early to get your towel supply for the day as they limit up to 5 towels per room. The restaurant (Marbella) was overpriced - $12 for a mediocre sandwich, and service was non-existent. If you are accustomed to service at restaurants in New York, be prepared to be disappointed. We only had dinner on our first night there because we were desperately tired. After that, we found better dining options at local restaurants outside the resort. The breakfast buffet was acceptable, for $18, it better be! Also, be prepared to pay $10 parking per day if you rented a car outside the resort (if you rented from Avis within the resort, you still have to pay $5 per day). The tour package offered by the hotel is again, overpriced. Unless you have no other option, skip them and go on your own. Also note, they're renovating the spa and laundry room, so if you need to do laundry on your own, you can't. However, they give 50% off the laundry service to compensate.

<Author>MonkeyFoot
<Content>Amazing Vacation My boyfriend and I just returned last night from a week at the Westin Rio Mar (August 8 - 14). This resort is wonderful. The grounds are beautiful and very well maintained. It's a great place to go if you enjoy golfing. However, even if you aren't there to golf (like us) you will have a great time. There are two very nice pools with plenty of lounge chairs and towels to go around. Althought the pools officially close at 8:00, we made a habit of taking a dip after dinner each night, as did others. In addition to the pools, there is easy access to the beach which is in very good condition. The water was a little rough a few days while we were there (strong rip tides) but definitely swimable and enjoyable. We had absolutely no problems with service. In fact, it was great. We had a broken t.v. when we arrived and it was exchanged with a new one within 15 minutes. We had room service daily and it always arrived before the estimated time. The staff was all very friendly and helpful. Our room was resort view and we had a very nice view of the pool area and the ocean in the background. We ate at all of the restaurants except for Palio's (which was no opened) and Ajili Mohili. All of the food was very good. My favorite was the Asian/Sushi restaurant. We also enjoyed the Grille Room. The food, however, was very pricey at all of the food establishments. This is the only complaint that I've read on Trip Advisor that I agree with. My boyfriend and I decided to pay the extra money and do the All Inclusive meal plan. It was more money but it was well worth the extra cost. We both loved the resort and had a great vacation. If you go make sure you visit the RainForest and I highly recommend the snorkeling trip on the catamaran. We had a wonderful time. We plan to return.

Our favorite was a pizza place- we can't remember the name, but it was just off the main highway, on the right hand side as you turn on the street to the resort- there is a candy shop right next to it. The bonus is that they deliver to the resort. We still crave this pizza!!!!!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A one week stay at the Westin We just returned from a one-week stay at the Westin -- a family vacation. I had read all the reviews extensively, about this hotel before leaving. The flavor that you get from reading these reviews is accurate. The hotel grounds and beach are first class. The beach privacy is perhaps its best feature. The beach is well-maintained, groomed every morning, and there were adequate chairs and beach umbrellas. The pools were beautiful, and very nice. The rooms are just average--not fancy by any stretch of the imagination. They are well soundproofed. They served well the only function that we could request of them -- a place to sleep. We found the staff to be friendly and polite and attentive. I was continually amazed at the check-in line at the front desk, every day. They are truly long waits regarding check-in. The price of drinks is unfortunately and unnecessarily ridiculous -- a glass of wine costs $10 and beach drinks --8.50. We did like the breakfast buffet (did that twice) which is served in the main facility-- at a price of $18 for adult and nine dollars for children (once my 19 and 16 year olds were childern--the other time adults; go figure). What we did for most breakfasts however was to buy boxes of dry cereal, local fruit, plastic bowls, plastic spoons, and purchase a large glass of fresh milk at the snack bar every morning. Much cheaper. They do have a nice outdoor lunch facility near the end of the larger pool for very nice sandwiches and french fries. Soft drink refills are free. The lunch menu items are about 10-12 dollars each, and splitting a sandwich provides ample portions. Cactus Jack's was only average, and expensive. The Grill was supposedly our fancy dinner for the vacation -- our last night. It was very stiff and formal. Entrees averaged about $40-- a total of $250 for four people and less than average quality. There is a nice shopping plaza in Fijardo--about a 15 minute drive further east from the Hotel, which has several choices for restaruants/dining/theaters at a much more affordable cost. I would definately rent a car from the airport (Hotwire), which we were able to get for 26$ a day. The additional $10 per day parking fee at the hotel is somewhat insulting, but seems to be standard these days. There is quite a great distance between parking and the hotel -- more than a five-minute walk. The hotel is directly across from the road that goes to the rain forest--which is free if you don't stop at the visitors center. We were able to drive into San Juan/Old San Juan without too much difficulty and is a definate must do-- it is approximately 30 minute drive. In Fijardo we were able to do a Bio Bay Kiak tour(you can bargin to get to a price of 25-30$ per person), and a separate cataraman snorkel excursion (Eastwind--59$ per person--lunch, drinks and gear provided--a 6 hour adventure). The concierge desk will give written directions about how to reach these places, and be sure that you get these directions. We found driving to be very confusing. The roads are narrow and often in poor condition. There is no such thing as a street sign anywhere, and we encountered difficulties in this respect on numerous occasions. The directions from the concierge desk will be very beneficial in that they are given in terms of stoplights and landmarks to allow you to get to your destination. Driving by yourself will save you substantial amounts of money in terms of the price that would cost if you arranged these functions through the hotel and their transportation. I have no regrets about this choice for lodging, and would stay there again. I would be happy to reply to questions/advice such as I am able to provide.

Also, not all restaurants are open all week, so if you have a preference to a certain restaurant, make sure you check when it is open when you arrive!Overall, we did not find this property on level of other Starwood properties we have stayed at. But we did enjoy the stay!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Beautiful resort; some complaints My husband and I just returned from a 4 day stay at the Westin. The hotel itself, the beach and the grounds are superior, absolutely gorgeous and immaculate. The beach especially is extremely well-maintained. They have ample chairs, some are cushioned, both alongside the beautiful pools and on the beach itself. But for a high-priced resort we were disappointed with a few points. The rooms are a bit sub-standard for a resort and the housekeeping is so-so (our maid forgot face towels entirely one day). The bathrooms were not spotless as you'd expect from a Westin. As well, this is a picky point, the hotel says that they deliver a newspaper to your room every morning, but none ever came. When I called to inquire, the concierge rudely said they had discontinued this service. I've never stayed in a Starwood or a comprable hotel where they didn't deliver a paper to your door every morning. The hotel literature provided, as well, is sadly out of date.The restaurants were ridiculously overpriced. The Grill Room was well-worth it as the food was excellent, but the other restaurants had below-average food. The Tiki Bar prices were insulting as well. We rented a car at the hotel and were forced to pay for hotel parking, which is just silly. At such a resort, to be nickel and dimed is just insulting. Also, avoid the tours the hotel offers. They are beyond ridiculous in terms of their prices. They charge $75 for a tour of the rainforest, when you can rent a car for that money, tour it leisurely on your own for free, and drive someplace else for dinner.As well, as the hotel is on a country club golf and tennis club, I suspect that many of the pool and beach occupants were club members' families. It is a kid friendly (albeit very expensive) place, but if you don't have kids and you don't like loud children in your quiet pool, avoid avoid avoid. There was never any quiet pool and the hottubs were constantly filled with children splashing about.We would not return.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Westin!!!!!! Don't trust all of the negative comments made by some travelers.....My husband and I recently stayed at the Westin and I want to provide you with an honest opinion - I highly recommend the Westin RioMar Resort. It is a large, beautifully landscaped property with all amenities one would desire for a great getaway. My husband and I stayed for 2 nights and enjoyed every moment - the only advice I can give is to bring some Off spray if you're prone to insect bites. The first night we walked out to the beach at approx. 6pm, sort of a humid evening, and I was surrounded by sea gnats. My husband did not get bit, but I managed to get over 100 bites on my legs and arms. Had no clue or would have prepared. I did make it out again the following day and there weren't any so depends on weather, but just be careful. Other than having a slow check-in, we thoroughly enjoyed our stay at this wonderful resort. The rooms are very nice and clean/comfortable, no outside noises were audible. The food was very good and adequately priced, although we did go outside of the resort as well (by the highway) to a Puerto Rican restaurant called Antojitos which was fantastic (try the fried Red Snapper). We also went to El Yunque Rainforest (great day trip!!). Then it was off to a great time in Old San Juan. You will be very pleased with your stay at the Westin RioMar - it is well worth it - I'm already planning a return trip there during the harsh winter here in Michigan!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Place to Vacation! Stayed April 21-25, had a wonderful vacation! The resort is beautiful, golf course is very nice, and the beach is wonderful - great for long walks, nice soft sand (yes, it's brown - but you're on the Atlantic Ocean side!), and the water is great - clear  a sand bottom great for playing  swimming. Our room was nice - we reserved a standard mountain view, but upon check-in we simply asked if there were any ocean views available and got upgraded for free! It never hurts to ask! Our room was very clean. It did smell a little musty - but hey, your in a tropical (Warm  Wet) climate - expect it! The fitness room needs some improvement - it is small and some of the equipment didn't work, but I got along ok as there weren't too many others in there at the same time. The casino is very small and cheesy - ok for the casual gambler. Service we had around the hotel at the front desk, consierge, bars, around the pool  beach, etc was very friendly and helpful. Service at the restaraunts, however, was slow so just expect to have dinner take a while. Our food was always very good. Arrange reservations for dinner w/ the consierge desk early in advance to get good times! There were always plenty of chairs on the beach, and more than enough towels available. Food  drinks aren't any more than any other Caribbean resort you'll go to - so just expect to pay for it!! If you are price sensitive on those things, maybe the Caribbean is not for you - go to Mexico. Overall we had an outstanding stay - the beach alone was well worth it! I've been all over the world, and this was a very nice place for the money. I've read many comments on several hotels - my advice to anyone is to slow down, relax (afterall, you're on vacation), and be nice. If you are nice and relaxed, you will get great service in return! Oh yeah, gratuity for the bell man and maids will be added to your bill automatically, so don't tip them each day unless you want to pay double. Anytime you want to avoid any surprises like that, when you check in just ask what you can expect to see on the bill at the end as far as hidden charges, etc. I will return to this resort!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We Would Return We stayed 7 nights All Inclusive (3/13-3/20)....After reading all of the negative reviews posted on this sight, my wife and I were very nervous about what to expect. We stayed for a week, under the All Inclusive Package, and had a wonderful, relaxing vacation(feel like I gained 10 pounds). The staff was pleasant and accomodating not once was the word No uttered when we had a request. Check in was smooth, we were given a free upgrade to a full ocean view, so be sure to ask. Room service took no more than 35 minutes. Juan at the breakfast buffet (Marbella) treated my family like we were part of his family (so much so that my 8 year old son was in tears the day we said goodbye). Henry and Ivan made sure that we always had a cold beverage at the Tikki Bar. They also made sure that our lunch was prepared in quick fashion. Dinner at Palio was wonderful...be sure to have Jesus as your waiter. Joelle tends bar right outside Palio, best bartender at the resort...I taught him how to make a great espresso martini, be sure to ask him for one. He noticed that my wife and I had reservations for a second night at Palio, he had my cigar and champagne ready for us ahead of time for that pre dinner cocktail. Cactus Jacks was disappointing, food was average at best, and our waiter there was definately a rookie. The pool area was delightful...The activity pool was perfect for the kids (14 and 8 years of age). Yet during peak time of year we thought the pool seemed quiet. There were plenty of chairs pool side. The pool deck is definately in need of repair/upgrade, and they could use a few more umbrellas as well as replacing some of the damaged ones. The beach was also fantastic. This is the Atlantic, not the Carribean Sea...yes there are waves, no the sand is not the white powder, yet still soft. Plenty of lounge chairs and Tikki Huts on the beach. Not once during our stay did I hear a complaint about not having a place to sit outdoors. What was also nice was the fact that the hotel/beach/pool area were very close to one another. We have stayed at other resorts where to get from point A to point B was sometimes quite a journey. This was very convenient...again especially for the kids. Restaurants....Palio thumbs way up; Shimas so/so; Cactus Jacks not worth the shuttle ride; Coqui just opened for dinner...very nice at night (poolside) with torches lit...still need to work out the kinks (dirty martini served as straight vodka no olives in a martini glass) but my porterhouse was terrific as was my wife's lobster. Marbella Buffet, surprisingly good for breakfast and lunch, two thumbs up again; room service also recd two thumbs up. other items mentioned in reviews....Bugs, never saw them....Wife got a few bites on the beach at night; towels, never a problem to get a fresh/dry towel, we would end up with 8 towels by the end of the day..no prob; prices, it's a resort wht do you expect to pay? Go with the All Inclusive....The exclusions are minimal, we certainly got our moneys worth and then some...Staff, no complaints see above; room, not musty, love the Westin beds, rooms do need a little updating, they do seem a bit old. No HBO? Missed the Sopranos. Lobby/Restaurants/Public areas were beautiful. Casino, dont make that the deciding factor. I dont gamble, but that casino was pretty comical. Definately for the small time/casual player. Food, better than Iberostar and other resorts that we have experienced. Night life, except for a couple of corny lounge/wedding singers there is nothing. many frustrated March Madness Fans could not find a place to watch the games. Nightlife = Eat + Drink + Gamble + Drink.....FYI, No free internet access...pay the $15.00 for high speed, dial up is considered a long distance call. OUCH!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good Times in PR My wife and I just returned from a week at the Westin RioMar in Beautiful PR. I read some of the reviews here before leaving and agree with some of what was said but would like to set the record straight on a number of things. First our room was very nice(not musty), pool and ocean view and the maid service was excellent. The food depending on the restaurant was good to excellent(I can't understand how people have complained about the food here), I highly recommend the Sea Bass at Ajili Mojili(authentic PR dishes) in the Ocean Villas and the Porterhouse steak at the GrilleRoom(located above the golf clubhouse, great views). KEY TIP: Find out early the days each restaurant is open during your stay and make reservations, it is very hard to walk-up and get a table even if the restaurant doesn't look full. The views of the rainforest were incredible, and there was lots of great nature sounds in the evening(The Coqui frogs!) One of the primary reasons we chose this resort was for the golf, and both courses are very nice but not spectacular, they charge $165 to play earlier in the day(way overpriced) but offer a twilight rate that starts at 2pm for $105(We booked our tee times in advance right at 2pm) the pace of play was great and you have incredible views of the mountains and plenty of wildlife(birds  iguanas of every size). The pools and ocean swimming are great just keep in mind the beach is brown sand and not white. If you are looking for lots of nightlife this is not the place for you, the only real nightlife is the small Casino(And I mean Small!) which is very poorly run. Overall the service at the resort was fairly good, a little inconsistent at times but not too bad, but the service in the Casino is terrible, the dealers and cashiers are not friendly and there are many slot machines not working properly and they don't know how to run a craps table(many payouts screwed up) and the cocktail waitresses in the casino are horrible they disappear for long stretches and one forgot to bring my drink twice and then finally brought me the wrong drink, you will end up going to the lobby bar for drinks, and it doesn't make sense because the casino is so small. We were looking for a scenic resort with good food to relax and play golf for a week. This resort fit the bill pretty well. If you don't play golf, and are looking for a wider range of activities I would recommend one of the many resorts in San Juan, but if you are looking for great views, good food, relaxing by the pool with a Pina Colada, and a few rounds of golf the Westin Rio Mar is an excellent choice.

<Author>lifelongNYER
<Content>Great place to stay! But keep in mind... The Westin was a beautiful hotel with friendly, courteous  extremely helpful staff. Upon arrival, check in went slow  we did get offered a below average room... however, after asking for an upgrade, we received one of the BEST rooms possible at no additional charge! The beach was private  beautiful however there is brown sand not white so those of you who feel it's dirty - it's not! It did get a little littered by the end of our 8-day stay but NOTHING to complain about. The pools were perfect - with the exception of no swim-up bar  although the tiki bar was great  VERY relaxing the hours were too limited. The food/restaurants at the hotel were well-above average - except that they were not always open so if you are looking to JUST be at the hotel the ENTIRE time you may want to take that into consideration. We rented an Avis car at the hotel (good price  cheap parking) and explored the island which we HIGHLY recommend doing! Don't expect 4-5 star areas or restaurants as you would find in the U.S. Mainland - but if you give it a chance you WILL find 4-5 star quality in both food  places to visit - ESPECIALLY with the people of P.R.!! The hotel is isolated so, for example, to get to San Juan is at least 40 minutes with a bit of traffic. We explored El Yunque which is a MUST! (GREAT tour through the Westin with Harry the tour guide!!). The East Wind Catamarran trip to Culebra is also HIGHLY recommended out of Fajardo. Luquillo beach is great but NOT in the public area of the beach!!! You must go INTO the area of Luquillo where seafood like King's  Sandy's are AMAZING  that area has the beautiful beaches. The kiosks off route 3 for Fast Puerto Rican Food seems scary but if you can get past what you are used to you will be in for a REAL TREAT!!! The Pina Colada's at La Roca Taina (#53 -#58?) out of the kiosks is awesome esp. for $3!!! And Hacienda Caribali for sunsets in Rio Grande overlooking El Yunque  Rio Mar was breathtaking! The food incredible - the service outstanding  again! THe Pina Coladas ROCKED!! Also - if you can muster up the energy - Old San Juan is truly magical... We ate at a local hideaway called El Jibarito (recommended in Frommer's) and it was some of the best Puerto Rican food we had on the island... For 2 meals  4 Medalla's (Puerto Rican beer) the bill was under $35 with tip. The main drawback to staying at the Westin Rio Mar is the lack of nightlife. If you don't mind driving a bit - the El Conquistador is good for some nightlife  Isla Verde is about 30 minutes away  GREAT for nightlife. For golf the Westin seems wonderful (we don't golf)  again, if isolation is a factor for your trip it's a TERRIFIC place to be! We were able to get both - relaxation  adventure  we can't WAIT to go back to Puerto Rico! Also for those people who we've read reviews of that complain about things like the humidity  bugs  sporadic rainstorms... It's a CARIBBEAN ISLAND! IT'S TROPICAL! DON'T GO IF YOU EXPECT TO FIND THIS OASIS OF PERFECT WEATHER! IT'S NOT POSSIBLE! And to us the weather was pretty perfect! Also, please keep in mind - Puerto Rico's MAIN language is SPANISH! 90% of the people speak english well but it helps to know a little spanish.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>"Heavenly 7" Package We stayed at the Westin Rio Mar from Jan.28 - Feb. 4, 2004 on their Heavenly 7 package. It certainly was just that: heavenly. Our room on the 7th floor was the concierge floor. This meant we were entitled to a daily continental breakfast of coffee, juice, fruit, toast, bagels, lox and sweet rolls. Our package also included buffet breadfast in the resort's main restaurant. So after an early continental breakfast, some sunning or shelling on the immaculate beach, we had a sumptuous buffet which carried us through lunch. Our floor served an afternoon snack of cookies, brownies, soda and coffee. From 5-8 PM was a wonderful spread of hot horsd'oevres, beer, wine, soda, veggies, crackers and cheeses. Most evenings, this was our supper.Our room was always cleaned promptly and had ample linens and toiletries. The housekeeping staff was friendly and accommodating! We had a problem with our AC vent and maintenance was there to remedy it within 5 mins. of our call.We found the beautifully landscaped grounds and the 3 pools very well maintained. There were ample towels available, plenty of chairs around the pools and on the beach.We only ate one dinner at the resort at Cactus Jacks. A bit pricey, but common for a resort. The food was excellent, the margaritas great. Drinks in the lobby bar and poolside were expensive, so we stuck to the free beer, wine and soda on our floor.The casino is very small at the resort and payouts are less than stateside casinos.Along with another couple, we rented a car for the week, having heard that taxies are expensive. Driving is a bit hectic, but the resort provided wonderful detailed directions.We all agreed that this was one of the best resorts we've ever experienced. The staff is exceptional, always friendly and helpful, and GOOD NATURED! We'd read some unfavorable reviews of bugs, musty rooms, unclean beach, unfriendly staff. We simply don't know how this is possible after experiencing the resort firsthand. We all decided we'd certainly return to the Westin Rio Mar without hesitation and highly recommend it.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Spectacular Beach My wife and I stayed at the Rio Mar for four nights the last week in January 2004. We loved it. The facilities at this hotel are exceptional. Our room was spacious and had a balcony with a view of EL Junque rainforest (the hotels grounds are located ten minutes from the park's entrance). Our accomodations were spacious, bright and clean. The grounds of the hotel (over 500 acres and 1 mile of beach) were splendidly landscaped and maintained. The two pools were large and little used. The beach was clean and raked every morning. Lounge chairs were readily available as were hammocks. On the grounds are two 18 hole golf courses, a jogging path, clubhouse, condos, tiki bars, a small casino and a spa. The resort has 7 restaurants including a gourmet Italian restaurant, an oriental restaurant and Marbella where you can order off the menu or partake in an upscale buffet in the evening. On balance we thought that the Westin Rio Mar was a very nice resort and would stay there agian. Other reviewers of the Rio Mar have complained about the food, the service, and the indifference of the employees. The food is expensive. What do you expect? This is not a cheap resort. You are paying for the view and the ambience and both are spectacular. I was extremely impressed with the attitude of the employees. Waiters, bartenders, blackjack dealers, cleaning staff, all greeted us warmly and attended to our needs promptly. Food quality at the Marbella was good but not exceptional. We did not eat at Palio or the oriental restaurant so I can't comment on their food. Some people have complained about the remoteness of the resort and those complaints are accurate. Just keep in mind that because the resort is 30 miles outside of San Juan, the beach is cleaner and less crowded and you don't have to deal with the congestion and pollution of the city. Easy sidetrips from this resort that were fun included El Junque rainforest, Luquillo Beach (food kiosks on the beach were exceptional), the city of Ponce (2 hr. to the south) and bar hopping in Penones. Also, just outside the grounds of the Westin Rio Mar there are several inexpensive restaurants serving good food.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A few bright lights but overall much worse than I expected There were some good things, and some really poor things about this place during my stay. The location next to the beach is nice. You can walk from your room pretty much right onto the beach. And the view as you do so is breathtaking. If you go, though, ASK ABOUT OCEAN VIEW ROOMS when you reserve your room. When we got there, we asked and none were available. The higher floors are better--pedestrians can see right into the lower floor rooms if the curtains are open. The hotel was very clean and attractive, although the ventilation in the room hallways was sometimes really bad, to where the air would be warm, humid, and smell bad. Service ranged from rarely good to almost uniformly HORRIBLE. We frequently waited long times either to get our orders taken or to get the check. Twice, I waited for a check for over 20 minutes after the plates were cleared, and I eventually had to find managers to get them. The waitstaff often refuse to make eye contact and gave me the impression that they felt like I was somehow beneath them. A few times we had genuinely nice people serve us or help us with our bags, and the concierge and front desk were always nice, but I cannot overstate this enough: be prepared for awful service more often than not. We were there a week and it was not just once or twice. The casino was also the same story--several times I waited over 20-30 minutes to get someone to come service the slot machine I played so it would pay out. Unless you get up and find someone, they will not come, despite the cameras in the ceiling. If you want free drinks, better sit at the table games. My wife and I sat at the slots for 2-3 hours on two separate nights and never saw a waitress, either. We were very surprised to find a brochure in the room that said that ALL casino patrons are entitled to free drinks after the experience of those two nights. We brought this up to the front desk and they comped us a breakfast buffet, which was nice. The food is sometimes pretty good; the Italian restaurant Palio was really good. But you are so isolated in the resort that if you do not have a rental car, you have to eat all your meals there. And believe me, they OVERCHARGE because they know you have no other options. A breakfast buffet is $18.50 per person. A dinner buffet (for average food--a chicken parmesan is boiled chicken breast, no breading, tomato sauce and a few shreds of parmesan cheese) is $30.00 per person. A virgin strawberry daquiri (essentially strawberries and ice) at the beach bar is $6.00. Another warning: the hotel bill will include gratuities that you are not told about. I had a $2.00 housekeeping gratuity per day tacked on, and this was after I had left some tips on the pillow because I didn't know about the gratuity. I had the bellhop bring up our bags and tipped them when they did so. Lo and behold, I ended up with a separate $12.00 Bell Service Gratuity on my bill for that day that no one had ever told me about. Overall, I enjoyed the beach. But if there had been another resort nearby, I would definitely try it the next time rather than go here again.

(We wished the sand was white like Turks and Caicos and the water clear but that's not the fault of the hotel--that's just P.R.) There were a few restaurants to choose from--all top quality with great service (not worth eating at Cactus Jack's Tex Mex though--overpriced for average food.) The best restaurants were the Grill for steak and Palio for Italian. Our room was cleaned beautifully every day and it was so large and plush that we felt right at home. Everyone was so helpful. The hotel felt very new and renovated. I would highly recommend this hotel if you just need a relaxing getaway. And did I mention the Spa? It's worth getting a facial or mini-massage (not worth the $ for the salt scrub) but great to know it was there if I wanted to go for more treatments. Really, really nice place.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>should have stayed at the el conquistador I just returned from a 4 day / 3 night stay at the Westin Rio Mar. Unfortunately, I do not have a lot of nice things to say about this resort. First off, our room was a bit on the small side and was not exactly the cleanliest room I've ever stayed in. The hotel staff definitely needs some training. As for the grounds, something needs to be done about the bugs / ants that are around the pool area. I couldn't even leave my shoes on the ground as the entire ground area was infested with ants. I have the bug bites to prove it - so please bring insect repellant if you do stay at this resort. The pools are not well maintained - I realize there will be bugs in the pool but it would help if someone actually skimmed the pool occasionally. If you are going to go to the Spa do not get a manicure  pedicure as they will charge you a $100 for both, the woman will cut your fingers and toes, and they do not have a pedicure chair or nail dryer. You'll also be placed in a small room without air conditioning. Forget about getting a late check-out. Our flight did not leave until 6:30 so we stayed at the hotel until 4 - we were allowed to shower at the Spa prior to leaving but there is no water pressure and I cannot say exactly when the last time these showers were cleaned but it is safe to say it's been a long time. The only thing that I can recommend is the Old San Juan shopping trip as well as eating at Cactus Jacks. Skip the outside restaurant near the activity pool. If you're going to leave the resort, try Isaura's Pizza down the hill from the hotel - it's really good. Just be careful who your cab driver is as one of our drivers did drive like a maniac.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>So-So Stay An interesting experience at the Westin Rio Mar. First and foremost, the bell staff, shuttle staff and valet staff were awesome! No complaints! The hotel, however, left a lot to be desired. To begin, I was reserved for double beds, traveling with my sister - booked into a king. Called for a roll-a-way, charged $35/night, although it was the hotel's error. (Nobody ever advised there was a pull-out sofa in the room until I disputed the charge). The main causal restaurant in the hotel was a great deal for lunch, but a TOTAL RIPOFF for dinner. They have buffet style, at almost $24, and the food wasn't even that good. We were seated outside where we were annoyed by stray cats and eaten alive by ants. Yay. The other restaurant we tried, Cactus Jacks, was a better value and the food was pretty good. Try the fajitas... but ask that they don't heat the skillet to the temperature of the sun. The casino has some of the tightest slots I've ever seen. Save your money for the tables. The concierge team was wonderful, but their directions aren't. We asked for driving directions to Bicardi Rum Factory and drove around in the vicinity for 30 minutes before giving up. Also, the business center didn't open as scheduled. It's a fair hotel, and FAR FROM THE AIRPORT.. about 40 minute drive with no traffic. Unless you want to get away from it all, stay closer to Old San Juan...thank me later.

<Rating>2	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A Palace in Paradise My wife and I stayed at the Westin Rio Mar for 4 nights in early October, 2003 and had one of the best vacations of our life. We enjoy traveling and have stayed at some truly exceptional hotels. The Westin Rio Mar ranks among the best that we have experienced. To name a couple high points, the service was excellent with every Westin employee greeting us with a smile. Our room, an upgraded junior suite with mountain view, was great on any scale. When compared with other carribian hotels, it far exceeded our expectations. The pools were great offering something for both families with kids and kid-free travelers. The beach was extraordinary, I highly recommend walks on the beach just after sunset, it really feels like you are walking in a movie.I read all of the reviews of this hotel prior to staying here and I can truly say I do not know why people complained about the quality and price of the restaurants. We ate at Palio, Marbella's, Ajili Mojili and the Coqui Lounge. Each was very good, with Palio's dinner and the seafood buffet at Marbella's topping the list. As far as price, IT IS A RESORT, food is not cheap. But $100 for dinner for two with drinks, $12-18 for breakfast buffet and ~$30-40 for lunch is par for the course. The food for those prices was very good.Finally, Puerto Rico is an wonderful island. Old San Juan combined elements from some of the most attractive cities I have ever seen. One recommendation, the Tapas restaurant at the El Coventeno hotel is out of sight, and is even better when you order a pitcher of sangria.I could not give a higher recommendation to the Westin or Puerto Rico.

<Content>Good but not only 3 !/2 stars For a supposed 5 star property we were not impressed, our rating 3 1/2, here's why. Cactus Jacks, food good, very large portions, pool table, bar. Note:Get a list of restaurant closing days and plan ahead. Off property recommendations: Metropol Restaurant in Fajardo 10 mins. Try dessert called Dirt a vanilla mousse secret recipe, we are going to try it at home. Marvelous menuand service. High speed trip to Flamenco Beach on Culebra Island on board an East Wind Excursions power catamaran, great. Negatives: Our room had a pedestal sink that was not connected to the wall tightly and when you leaned on it or bumped into it there was an annoyingly loud sound that would disturb any sleepers in the room. the maintenance people were in over their heads on this one and we gave up. We must add: All the people we came into contact with were a joy to deal with, one moreso than the other. Puerto Ricans are a wonderful people! We spent a long time touring in our week there and never had a bad experience, all you do is ask for help. Caution: Driving is wild unless you are used to New York City and off the major roads there are only a few road signs, get good directions. ps:Smoke in the lobby outside the casino and smoke everywhere inside. Do the bio-bay trip.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Definitely not worth the $$$ I was not terribly impressed with this property. We just stayed there for four nights in mid-June. My wife is a Starwood Platinum, so we did receive an upgrade to an Ocean Suite room but not much else. The room was ok, probably better than the standard rooms, but very musty and worn. We found the some of the employees to be lacking as well. When we arrived, we pulled to the front of the hotel, asked one of the employees for the location of self parking. He was more concerned with the luggage in our car than our question, and when it was apparent that he wasn't going to make a tip, turned around and walked off without the courtesy of answering the question. That set the basic tone of our stay. Club lounge apparently was not available due to being off season, so no access there. Minor items that should go without thought such as providing adequate soap for the shower was not done. (1 bar for the total 4 night stay for 2 people). We have generally had great experiences with Starwood properties, however, definitely will not go back to this one. Even simple things like internet access are a pain at this property. If you bring your own computer, and your ISP access number is in San Juan, be prepared to pay $2.00 PER MINUTE in addition to the usual phone access charge. Want to use the business center, better do it before 5:00 pm, and be prepared to pay $20/hr for internet access. Want to use a cell phone to circumvent the ridiculous hotel phone charges? Here's a new one. When we attempted to use an ATT cell phone on the property, a secondary tone comes on the line for something called Roaming America, attempting to get you to provide a credit card number for an additional charge to complete your call. Drive a quarter mile away, or go anywhere else on the island, you get connected as usual with ATT. The front desk denied any knowledge of any of this, however you look at the top of the hotel building you see cell phone antennas, so draw your own conclusions. Fortunately we were in Puerto Rico on business, so spent little time at the property, and after all of this was determined not to spend one dime beyond the room, tax, resort fee and parking, so we entertained and took meals away from the resort. Next year we will return to the Caribe Hilton. Stayed there last year as Hilton Gold, was treated much better, had a great time. I definitely feel that there are major staff problems. Some staff at this property appeared to be indifferent, particularly if they were not going to make a tip from you. One staff member in the parking lot was even argumentative over something very insignificant. I definitely detected a real attitude from some of the staff at this property, and I am a person of reasonable expectations and I rarely complain, so I don't think it is just me. Your money is much better spent elsewhere. Additionally, this property is more than 30 miles from San Juan, but it is not a quick 30 mile drive as you would expect in the mainland U.S. It is a very hectic and stressful 30+ miles on substandard roads with some of the worst driving I have ever seen in my life. Definitely something to take into consideration if you plan to go to San Juan during your stay.  
<Date>Jun 24, 2003
<Rating>1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	-1	

<Author>ejan
<Content>Nice Resort, Suggestions We stayed at the Westin Rio Mar over Easter Vacation. The place is beautiful, the service is good. The rooms are really nice with all the amenities. I booked two connecting rooms (we have older kids), and there was no problem with that because I was able to pre-check-in by calling the hotel directly that morning. Another suggestion: make your dinner reservations in advance (even from home) so there won't be a problem. The good times for the restaurants fill up fast. Also, the hotel's car rental sold out, but the conceirge was able to help us book a car off the premises (for less $). The rain forest is a must see, but I would recommend renting a car and going yourself. The drive is very easy from the hotel, and once you're there, you'll want the flexibility of hiking at your leisure. When booking this hotel, try to get the breakfast included, and ask for promotional rates. We got the big breakfast buffet, transfers, all tax and service charge included plus the 5th night free (for $290 a room, that's it). Many people paid a lot more. Also, the hotel's sunset sail trip was very nice. I'd recommend that.
